produce by juliet sutherland david garcium and the online distribute proofread team a compilation of the message and papers of the president by jame d richardson jame buchanan march 4 1857 to march 4 1861 jame buchanan jame buchanan be bear near mercersburg pa April 23 1791 he father jame buchanan a scotch-irish farmer come from the county of donegal ireland in 1783 he mother be elizabeth speer the future president be educate at a school in mercersburg and at dickinson college pennsylvanium where he be graduate in 1809 begin to practice law in lancaster in 1812 he first public address be make at the age of 23 on the occasion of a popular meeting in lancaster after the capture of washington by the british in 1814 although a federalist and with he party oppose to the war he urge the enlistment of volunteer for the defense of baltimore and be among the first to enroll he name in October 1814 be elect to the legislature of pennsylvanium for lancaster county and again elect in 1815 at the close of he term in the legislature retire to the practice of the law gain early distinction in 1820 be elect to congress to represent a district compose of lancaster york and dauphin county and take he seat in December 1821 he be call a federalist but the party distinction of that time be not clearly define and mr buchanan 's political principle as a national statesman be yet to be form he first speech in congress be make in January 1822 sustain the administration of president monroe and of john c calhoun secretary of war in particular with reference to a military establishment president monroe 's veto in may 1822 of a bill impose toll for the support of the cumberland road for which mr buchanan have vote produce a strong effect upon he constitutional view and he begin to perceive the divide line between the federal and the state power he remain in the house of representative ten year -- during mr monroe 's second term through the administration of john quincy adam and during the first two year of jackson 's administration in December 1829 become chairman of the judiciary committee of the house during mr adam 's term the friend of the administration begin to take the name of national republican while the oppose party assume the name of democrat mr buchanan be one of the leader of the opposition in the house of representative be always a strong supporter and warm personal friend of general jackson in march 1831 at the close of the twenty-first congress it be mr buchanan 's wish to retire from public life but at the request of president jackson he accept the mission to russium negotiate a commercial treaty with that country August 8 1833 leave st petersburg spend a short time in pari and london and reach home in November in 1834 be appoint one of the commissioner on the part of pennsylvanium to arrange with commissioner from new jersey concern the use of the water of the delaware river December 6 1834 be elect to the united state senate to fill a vacancy and be reelect in January 1837 be conspicuous in the senate as a supporter of jackson 's financial policy throughout he administration and that of he successor mr van buren of the same party in 1839 decline the office of attorney-general tender by president van buren in 1843 be elect to the senate for a third term and in 1844 he name be bring forward as the democratic candidate of pennsylvanium for the presidential nomination but before the national convention meet he withdraw he name at the beginning of the administration of jame k polk become secretary of state and as such have a number of important question to deal with include the settlement of the boundary between oregon territory and the british possession and the annexation of texa which result in the mexican war on the accession of mr taylor to the presidency mr buchanan retire for a time from official life be a unsuccessful candidate for the presidential nomination before the democratic national convention June 1 1852 in April 1853 be appoint minister to england by president pierce be recall at he own request in 1855 June 3 1856 be nominate for president of the united state by the democratic national convention at cincinnatus ohio and on November 4 1856 be elect receive 174 electoral vote to 114 for john c fremont and 8 for millard fillmore be inaugurate march 4 1857 in 1860 refuse the use of he name for renomination at the conclusion of he term return to he home at wheatland near lancaster pa die June 1 1868 and be bury at wheatland inaugural address fellow-citizen : i appear before you this day to take the solemn oath that i will faithfully execute the office of president of the united state and will to the best of my ability preserve protect and defend the constitution of the united state in enter upon this great office i must humbly invoke the god of we father for wisdom and firmness to execute its high and responsible duty in such a manner as to restore harmony and ancient friendship among the people of the several state and to preserve we free institution throughout many generation convince that i owe my election to the inherent love for the constitution and the union which still animate the heart of the american people let I earnestly ask they powerful support in sustain all just measure calculate to perpetuate these the richest political blessing which heaven have ever bestow upon any nation have determine not to become a candidate for reelection i shall have no motive to influence my conduct in administer the government except the desire ably and faithfully to serve my country and to live in the grateful memory of my countryman we have recently pass through a presidential contest in which the passion of we fellow-citizen be excite to the highest degree by question of deep and vital importance but when the people proclaim they will the tempest at once subside and all be calm the voice of the majority speaking in the manner prescribe by the constitution be hear and instant submission follow we own country could alone have exhibit so grand and striking a spectacle of the capacity of man for self-government what a happy conception then be it for congress to apply this simple rule that the will of the majority shall govern to the settlement of the question of domestic slavery in the territory congress be neither to legislate slavery into any territory or state nor to exclude it therefrom but to leave the people thereof perfectly free to form and regulate they domestic institution in they own way subject only to the constitution of the united state as a natural consequence congress have also prescribe that when the territory of kansas shall be admit as a state it shall be receive into the union with or without slavery as they constitution may prescribe at the time of they admission a difference of opinion have arise in regard to the point of time when the people of a territory shall decide this question for themselves this be happily a matter of but little practical importance besides it be a judicial question which legitimately belong to the supreme court of the united state before whom it be now pend and will it be understand be speedily and finally settle to they decision in common with all good citizen i shall cheerfully submit whatever this may be though it have ever be my individual opinion that under the nebraska-kansas act the appropriate period will be when the number of actual resident in the territory shall justify the formation of a constitution with a view to its admission as a state into the union but be this as it may it be the imperative and indispensable duty of the government of the united state to secure to every resident inhabitant the free and independent expression of he opinion by he vote this sacred right of each individual must be preserve that be accomplish nothing can be fairer than to leave the people of a territory free from all foreign interference to decide they own destiny for themselves subject only to the constitution of the united state the whole territorial question be thus settle upon the principle of popular sovereignty -- a principle as ancient as free government itself -- everything of a practical nature have be decide no other question remain for adjustment because all agree that under the constitution slavery in the state be beyond the reach of any human power except that of the respective state themselves wherein it exist may we not then hope that the long agitation on this subject be approach its end and that the geographical party to which it have give birth so much dread by the father of he country will speedily become extinct most happy will it be for the country when the public mind shall be divert from this question to other of more press and practical importance throughout the whole progress of this agitation which have scarcely know any intermission for more than twenty year whilst it have be productive of no positive good to any human be it have be the prolific source of great evil to the master to the slave and to the whole country it have alienate and estrange the people of the sister state from each other and have even seriously endanger the very existence of the union nor have the danger yet entirely cease under we system there be a remedy for all mere political evil in the sound sense and sober judgment of the people time be a great corrective political subject which but a few year ago excited and exasperate the public mind have pass away and be now nearly forget but this question of domestic slavery be of far graver importance than any mere political question because should the agitation continue it may eventually endanger the personal safety of a large portion of we countryman where the institution exist in that event no form of government however admirable in itself and however productive of material benefit can compensate for the loss of peace and domestic security around the family altar let every union-loving man therefore exert he best influence to suppress this agitation which since the recent legislation of congress be without any legitimate object it be a evil omen of the time that man have undertake to calculate the mere material value of the union reason estimate have be present of the pecuniary profit and local advantage which would result to different state and section from its dissolution and of the comparative injury which such a event would inflict on other state and section even descend to this low and narrow view of the mighty question all such calculation be at fault the bare reference to a single consideration will be conclusive on this point we at present enjoy a free trade throughout we extensive and expand country such as the world have never witness this trade be conduct on railroad and canal on noble river and arm of the sea which bind together the north and the south the east and the west of we confederacy annihilate this trade arrest its free progress by the geographical line of jealous and hostile state and you destroy the prosperity and onward march of the whole and every part and involve all in one common ruin but such consideration important as they be in themselves sink into insignificance when we reflect on the terrific evil which would result from disunion to every portion of the confederacy -- to the north not more than to the south to the east not more than to the west these i shall not attempt to portray because i feel a humble confidence that the kind providence which inspire we father with wisdom to frame the most perfect form of government and union ever devise by man will not suffer it to perish until it shall have be peacefully instrumental by its example in the extension of civil and religious liberty throughout the world next in importance to the maintenance of the constitution and the union be the duty of preserve the government free from the taint or even the suspicion of corruption public virtue be the vital spirit of republic and history prove that when this have decay and the love of money have usurp its place although the form of free government may remain for a season the substance have depart forever we present financial condition be without a parallel in history no nation have ever before be embarrass from too large a surplus in its treasury this almost necessarily give birth to extravagant legislation it produce wild scheme of expenditure and beget a race of speculator and jobber whose ingenuity be exert in contrive and promote expedient to obtain public money the purity of official agent whether rightfully or wrongfully be suspect and the character of the government suffer in the estimation of the people this be in itself a very great evil the natural mode of relief from this embarrassment be to appropriate the surplus in the treasury to great national object for which a clear warrant can be find in the constitution among these i might mention the extinguishment of the public debt a reasonable increase of the navy which be at present inadequate to the protection of we vast tonnage afloat now greater than that of any other nation as well as to the defense of we extended seacoast it be beyond all question the true principle that no more revenue ought to be collect from the people than the amount necessary to defray the expense of a wise economical and efficient administration of the government to reach this point it be necessary to resort to a modification of the tariff and this have i trust be accomplish in such a manner as to do as little injury as may have be practicable to we domestic manufacture especially those necessary for the defense of the country any discrimination against a particular branch for the purpose of benefit favored corporation individual or interest would have be unjust to the rest of the community and inconsistent with that spirit of fairness and equality which ought to govern in the adjustment of a revenue tariff but the squander of the public money sink into comparative insignificance as a temptation to corruption when compare with the squander of the public land no nation in the tide of time have ever be bless with so rich and noble a inheritance as we enjoy in the public land in administer this important trust whilst it may be wise to grant portion of they for the improvement of the remainder yet we should never forget that it be we cardinal policy to reserve these land as much as may be for actual settler and this at moderate price we shall thus not only best promote the prosperity of the new state and territory by furnish they a hardy and independent race of honest and industrious citizen but shall secure home for we child and we child 's child as well as for those exile from foreign shore who may seek in this country to improve they condition and to enjoy the blessing of civil and religious liberty such emigrant have do much to promote the growth and prosperity of the country they have prove faithful both in peace and in war after become citizen they be entitle under the constitution and law to be place on a perfect equality with native-born citizen and in this character they should ever be kindly recognize the federal constitution be a grant from the state to congress of certain specific power and the question whether this grant should be liberally or strictly construe have more or less divide political party from the beginning without enter into the argument i desire to state at the commencement of my administration that long experience and observation have convince I that a strict construction of the power of the government be the only true as well as the only safe theory of the constitution whenever in we past history doubtful power have be exercise by congress these have never fail to produce injurious and unhappy consequence many such instance might be adduce if this be the proper occasion neither be it necessary for the public service to strain the language of the constitution because all the great and useful power require for a successful administration of the government both in peace and in war have be grant either in express term or by the plainest implication whilst deeply convinced of these truth i yet consider it clear that under the war-making power congress may appropriate money toward the construction of a military road when this be absolutely necessary for the defense of any state or territory of the union against foreign invasion under the constitution congress have power to declare war to raise and support army to provide and maintain a navy and to call forth the militia to repel invasion thus endowed in a ample manner with the war-making power the corresponding duty be require that the united state shall protect each of they -lrb- the state -rrb- against invasion now how be it possible to afford this protection to californium and we pacific possession except by means of a military road through the territory of the united state over which man and munitions of war may be speedily transport from the atlantic state to meet and to repel the invader in the event of a war with a naval power much stronger than we own we should then have no other available access to the pacific coast because such a power would instantly close the route across the isthmus of central america it be impossible to conceive that whilst the constitution have expressly require congress to defend all the state it should yet deny to they by any fair construction the only possible means by which one of these state can be defend besides the government ever since its origin have be in the constant practice of construct military road it might also be wise to consider whether the love for the union which now animate we fellow-citizen on the pacific coast may not be impair by we neglect or refusal to provide for they in they remote and isolate condition the only means by which the power of the state on this side of the rocky mountain can reach they in sufficient time to protect they against invasion i forbear for the present from express a opinion as to the wisest and most economical mode in which the government can lend its aid in accomplish this great and necessary work i believe that many of the difficulty in the way which now appear formidable will in a great degree vanish as soon as the nearest and best route shall have be satisfactorily ascertain it may be proper that on this occasion i should make some brief remark in regard to we rights and duty as a member of the great family of nation in we intercourse with they there be some plain principle approve by we own experience from which we should never depart we ought to cultivate peace commerce and friendship with all nation and this not merely as the best means of promote we own material interest but in a spirit of christian benevolence toward we fellow-men wherever they lot may be cast we diplomacy should be direct and frank neither seek to obtain more nor accept less than be we due we ought to cherish a sacred regard for the independence of all nation and never attempt to interfere in the domestic concern of any unless this shall be imperatively require by the great law of self-preservation to avoid entangle alliance have be a maxim of we policy ever since the day of washington and its wisdom no one will attempt to dispute in short we ought to do justice in a kindly spirit to all nation and require justice from they in return it be we glory that whilst other nation have extend they dominion by the sword we have never acquire any territory except by fair purchase or as in the case of texa by the voluntary determination of a brave kindred and independent people to blend they destiny with we own even we acquisition from mexico form no exception unwilling to take advantage of the fortune of war against a sister republic we purchase these possession under the treaty of peace for a sum which be consider at the time a fair equivalent we past history forbid that we shall in the future acquire territory unless this be sanction by the law of justice and honor act on this principle no nation will have a right to interfere or to complain if in the progress of event we shall still further extend we possession hitherto in all we acquisition the people under the protection of the american flag have enjoy civil and religious liberty as well as equal and just law and have be contented prosperous and happy they trade with the rest of the world have rapidly increase and thus every commercial nation have share largely in they successful progress i shall now proceed to take the oath prescribe by the constitution whilst humbly invoke the blessing of divine providence on this great people march 4 1857 first annual message washington _ December 8 1857 _ _ fellow-citizen of the senate and house of representative _ : in obedience to the command of the constitution it have now become my duty to give to congress information of the state of the union and recommend to they consideration such measure as i judge to be necessary and expedient but first and above all we thanks be due to almighty god for the numerous benefit which he have bestow upon this people and we unite prayer ought to ascend to he that he would continue to bless we great republic in time to come as he have bless it in time past since the adjournment of the last congress we constituent have enjoy a unusual degree of health the earth have yield she fruit abundantly and have bountifully reward the toil of the husbandman we great staple have command high price and up till within a brief period we manufacturing mineral and mechanical occupation have largely partake of the general prosperity we have possess all the element of material wealth in rich abundance and yet notwithstanding all these advantage we country in its monetary interest be at the present moment in a deplorable condition in the midst of unsurpassed plenty in all the production of agriculture and in all the element of national wealth we find we manufacture suspend we public work retard we private enterprise of different kind abandon and thousand of useful laborer throw out of employment and reduce to want the revenue of the government which be chiefly derive from duty on import from abroad have be greatly reduce whilst the appropriation make by congress at its last session for the current fiscal year be very large in amount under these circumstance a loan may be require before the close of you present session but this although deeply to be regret would prove to be only a slight misfortune when compare with the suffering and distress prevail among the people with this the government can not fail deeply to sympathize though it may be without the power to extend relief it be we duty to inquire what have produce such unfortunate result and whether they recurrence can be prevent in all former revulsion the blame might have be fairly attribute to a variety of cooperate cause but not so upon the present occasion it be apparent that we exist misfortune have proceed solely from we extravagant and vicious system of paper currency and bank credit exciting the people to wild speculation and gamble in stock these revulsion must continue to recur at successive interval so long as the amount of the paper currency and bank loan and discount of the country shall be leave to the discretion of 1400 irresponsible banking institution which from the very law of they nature will consult the interest of they stockholder rather than the public welfare the framer of the constitution when they give to congress the power to coin money and to regulate the value thereof and prohibit the state from coin money emit bill of credit or make anything but gold and silver coin a tender in payment of debt suppose they have protect the people against the evil of a excessive and irredeemable paper currency they be not responsible for the exist anomaly that a government endowed with the sovereign attribute of coin money and regulate the value thereof should have no power to prevent other from drive this coin out of the country and fill up the channel of circulation with paper which do not represent gold and silver it be one of the highest and most responsible duty of government to insure to the people a sound circulate medium the amount of which ought to be adapt with the utmost possible wisdom and skill to the want of internal trade and foreign exchange if this be either greatly above or greatly below the proper standard the marketable value of every man 's property be increase or diminish in the same proportion and injustice to individual as well as incalculable evil to the community be the consequence unfortunately under the construction of the federal constitution which have now prevail too long to be change this important and delicate duty have be dissever from the coin power and virtually transfer to more than 1400 state bank act independently of each other and regulate they paper issue almost exclusively by a regard to the present interest of they stockholder exercise the sovereign power of provide a paper currency instead of coin for the country the first duty which these bank owe to the public be to keep in they vault a sufficient amount of gold and silver to insure the convertibility of they note into coin at all time and under all circumstance no bank ought ever to be charter without such restriction on its business as to secure this result all other restriction be comparatively vain this be the only true touchstone the only efficient regulator of a paper currency -- the only one which can guard the public against overissue and bank suspension as a collateral and eventual security it be doubtless wise and in all case ought to be require that bank shall hold a amount of united state or state security equal to they note in circulation and pledge for they redemption this however furnish no adequate security against overissue on the contrary it may be pervert to inflate the currency indeed it be possible by this mean to convert all the debt of the united state and state government into bank note without reference to the specie require to redeem they however valuable these security may be in themselves they can not be convert into gold and silver at the moment of pressure as we experience teach in sufficient time to prevent bank suspension and the depreciation of bank note in england which be to a considerable extent a paper-money country though vastly behind we own in this respect it be deem advisable anterior to the act of parliament of 1844 which wisely separate the issue of note from the banking department for the bank of england always to keep on hand gold and silver equal to one-third of its combined circulation and deposit if this proportion be no more than sufficient to secure the convertibility of its note with the whole of great britain and to some extent the continent of europe as a field for its circulation render it almost impossible that a sudden and immediate run to a dangerous amount should be make upon it the same proportion would certainly be insufficient under we banking system each of we 1400 bank have but a limited circumference for its circulation and in the course of a very few day the depositor and note holder might demand from such a bank a sufficient amount in specie to compel it to suspend even although it have coin in its vault equal to one-third of its immediate liability and yet i be not aware with the exception of the bank of louisiana that any state bank throughout the union have be require by its charter to keep this or any other proportion of gold and silver compare with the amount of its combined circulation and deposit what have be the consequence in a recent report make by the treasury department on the condition of the bank throughout the different state accord to return date nearest to January 1857 the aggregate amount of actual specie in they vault be $ 58349838 of they circulation $ 214778822 and of they deposit $ 230351352 thus it appear that these bank in the aggregate have considerably less than one dollar in seven of gold and silver compare with they circulation and deposit it be palpable therefore that the very first pressure must drive they to suspension and deprive the people of a convertible currency with all its disastrous consequence it be truly wonderful that they should have so long continue to preserve they credit when a demand for the payment of one-seventh of they immediate liability would have drive they into insolvency and this be the condition of the bank notwithstanding that four hundred million of gold from californium have flow in upon we within the last eight year and the tide still continue to flow indeed such have be the extravagance of bank credit that the bank now hold a considerably less amount of specie either in proportion to they capital or to they circulation and deposit combine than they do before the discovery of gold in californium whilst in the year 1848 they specie in proportion to they capital be more than equal to one dollar for four and a half in 1857 it do not amount to one dollar for every six dollar and thirty-three cent of they capital in the year 1848 the specie be equal within a very small fraction to one dollar in five of they circulation and deposit in 1857 it be not equal to one dollar in seven and a half of they circulation and deposit from this statement it be easy to account for we financial history for the last forty year it have be a history of extravagant expansion in the business of the country follow by ruinous contraction at successive interval the best and most enterprising man have be tempt to they ruin by excessive bank loan of mere paper credit exciting they to extravagant importation of foreign goods wild speculation and ruinous and demoralizing stock gambling when the crisis arrive as arrive it must the bank can extend no relief to the people in a vain struggle to redeem they liability in specie they be compel to contract they loan and they issue and at last in the hour of distress when they assistance be most need they and they debtor together sink into insolvency it be this paper system of extravagant expansion raise the nominal price of every article far beyond its real value when compare with the cost of similar article in country whose circulation be wisely regulate which have prevent we from compete in we own market with foreign manufacturer have produce extravagant importation and have counteract the effect of the large incidental protection afford to we domestic manufacture by the present revenue tariff but for this the branch of we manufacture compose of raw material the production of we own country -- such as cotton iron and woolen fabric -- would not only have acquire almost exclusive possession of the home market but would have create for themselves a foreign market throughout the world deplorable however as may be we present financial condition we may yet indulge in bright hope for the future no other nation have ever exist which could have endure such violent expansion and contraction of paper credit without last injury yet the buoyancy of youth the energy of we population and the spirit which never quail before difficulty will enable we soon to recover from we present financial embarrassment and may even occasion we speedily to forget the lesson which they have teach in the meantime it be the duty of the government by all proper means within its power to aid in alleviate the suffering of the people occasion by the suspension of the bank and to provide against a recurrence of the same calamity unfortunately in either aspect of the case it can do but little thanks to the independent treasury the government have not suspend payment as it be compel to do by the failure of the bank in 1837 it will continue to discharge its liability to the people in gold and silver its disbursement in coin will pass into circulation and materially assist in restore a sound currency from its high credit should we be compel to make a temporary loan it can be effect on advantageous term this however shall if possible be avoid but if not then the amount shall be limit to the lowest practicable sum i have therefore determine that whilst no useful government work already in progress shall be suspend new work not already commence will be postpone if this can be do without injury to the country those necessary for its defense shall proceed as though there have be no crisis in we monetary affair but the federal government can not do much to provide against a recurrence of exist evil even if insurmountable constitutional objection do not exist against the creation of a national bank this would furnish no adequate preventive security the history of the last bank of the united state abundantly prove the truth of this assertion such a bank could not if it would regulate the issue and credit of 1400 state bank in such a manner as to prevent the ruinous expansion and contraction in we currency which afflict the country throughout the existence of the late bank or secure we against future suspension in 1825 a effort be make by the bank of england to curtail the issue of the country bank under the most favorable circumstance the paper currency have be expand to a ruinous extent and the bank put forth all its power to contract it in order to reduce price and restore the equilibrium of the foreign exchange it accordingly commence a system of curtailment of its loan and issue in the vain hope that the joint stock and private bank of the kingdom would be compel to follow its example it find however that as it contract they expand and at the end of the process to employ the language of a very high official authority whatever reduction of the paper circulation be effect by the bank of england -lrb- in 1825 -rrb- be more than make up by the issue of the country bank but a bank of the united state would not if it could restrain the issue and loan of the state bank because its duty as a regulator of the currency must often be in direct conflict with the immediate interest of its stockholder if we expect one agent to restrain or control another they interest must at least in some degree be antagonistic but the director of a bank of the united state would feel the same interest and the same inclination with the director of the state bank to expand the currency to accommodate they favorite and friend with loan and to declare large dividend such have be we experience in regard to the last bank after all we must mainly rely upon the patriotism and wisdom of the state for the prevention and redress of the evil if they will afford we a real specie basis for we paper circulation by increase the denomination of bank note first to twenty and afterwards to fifty dollar if they will require that the bank shall at all time keep on hand at least one dollar of gold and silver for every three dollar of they circulation and deposit and if they will provide by a self-executing enactment which nothing can arrest that the moment they suspend they shall go into liquidation i believe that such provision with a weekly publication by each bank of a statement of its condition would go far to secure we against future suspension of specie payment congress in my opinion possess the power to pass a uniform bankrupt law applicable to all banking institution throughout the united state and i strongly recommend its exercise this would make it the irreversible organic law of each bank 's existence that a suspension of specie payment shall produce its civil death the instinct of self-preservation would then compel it to perform its duty in such a manner as to escape the penalty and preserve its life the existence of bank and the circulation of bank paper be so identify with the habit of we people that they can not at this day be suddenly abolish without much immediate injury to the country if we could confine they to they appropriate sphere and prevent they from administer to the spirit of wild and reckless speculation by extravagant loan and issue they might be continue with advantage to the public but this i say after long and much reflection : if experience shall prove it to be impossible to enjoy the facility which well-regulated bank might afford without at the same time suffer the calamity which the excess of the bank have hitherto inflict upon the country it would then be far the lesser evil to deprive they altogether of the power to issue a paper currency and confine they to the function of bank of deposit and discount we relation with foreign government be upon the whole in a satisfactory condition the diplomatic difficulty which exist between the government of the united state and that of great britain at the adjournment of the last congress have be happily terminate by the appointment of a british minister to this country who have be cordially receive whilst it be greatly to the interest as i be convinced it be the sincere desire of the government and people of the two country to be on term of intimate friendship with each other it have be we misfortune almost always to have have some irritating if not dangerous outstanding question with great britain since the origin of the government we have be employ in negotiate treaty with that power and afterwards in discuss they true intent and meaning in this respect the convention of April 19 1850 commonly call the clayton and bulwer treaty have be the most unfortunate of all because the two government place directly opposite and contradictory construction upon its first and most important article whilst in the united state we believe that this treaty would place both power upon a exact equality by the stipulation that neither will ever occupy or fortify or colonize or assume or exercise any dominion over any part of central america it be contend by the british government that the true construction of this language have leave they in the rightful possession of all that portion of central america which be in they occupancy at the date of the treaty in fact that the treaty be a virtual recognition on the part of the united state of the right of great britain either as owner or protector to the whole extensive coast of central america sweeping round from the rio hondo to the port and harbor of san juan de nicaragua together with the adjacent bay island except the comparatively small portion of this between the sarstoon and cape hondura accord to they construction the treaty do no more than simply prohibit they from extend they possession in central america beyond the present limit it be not too much to assert that if in the united state the treaty have be consider susceptible of such a construction it never would have be negotiate under the authority of the president nor would it have receive the approbation of the senate the universal conviction in the united state be that when we government consent to violate its traditional and time-honored policy and to stipulate with a foreign government never to occupy or acquire territory in the central american portion of we own continent the consideration for this sacrifice be that great britain should in this respect at least be place in the same position with ourselves whilst we have no right to doubt the sincerity of the british government in they construction of the treaty it be at the same time my deliberate conviction that this construction be in opposition both to its letter and its spirit under the late administration negotiation be institute between the two government for the purpose if possible of remove these difficulty and a treaty have this laudable object in view be sign at london on the 17th October 1856 and be submit by the president to the senate on the follow 10th of December whether this treaty either in its original or amend form would have accomplish the object intend without give birth to new and embarrassing complication between the two government may perhaps be well question certain it be however it be render much less objectionable by the different amendment make to it by the senate the treaty as amend be ratify by I on the 12th march 1857 and be transmit to london for ratification by the british government that government express its willingness to concur in all the amendment make by the senate with the single exception of the clause relate to ruatan and the other island in the bay of hondura the article in the original treaty as submit to the senate after recite important domestic institution should or should not continue to exist indeed this be the only possible mode in which they will could be authentically ascertain the election of delegate to a convention must necessarily take place in separate district from this cause it may readily happen as have often be the case that a majority of the people of a state or territory be on one side of a question whilst a majority of the representative from the several district into which it be divide may be upon the other side this arise from the fact that in some district delegate may be elect by small majority whilst in other those of different sentiment may receive majority sufficiently great not only to overcome the vote give for the former but to leave a large majority of the whole people in direct opposition to a majority of the delegate besides we history prove that influence may be bring to bear on the representative sufficiently powerful to induce he to disregard the will of he constituent the truth be that no other authentic and satisfactory mode exist of ascertain the will of a majority of the people of any state or territory on a important and exciting question like that of slavery in kansas except by leave it to a direct vote how wise then be it for congress to pass over all subordinate and intermediate agency and proceed directly to the source of all legitimate power under we institution how vain would any other principle prove in practice this may be illustrate by the case of kansa should she be admit into the union with a constitution either maintain or abolish slavery against the sentiment of the people this could have no other effect than to continue and to exasperate the exist agitation during the brief period require to make the constitution this be the first rebellion which have exist in we territory and humanity itself require that we should put it down in such a manner that it shall be the last to trifle with it would be to encourage congress cost what it may in suppress the insurrection and in restore and maintain the sovereignty of the constitution and law over the territory of utah i recommend to congress the establishment of a be now carry over it throughout its whole extent and this route be know to be the nearest and believe to be the best to the pacific long experience have deeply convinced I that a strict construction of the power grant to congress be the only true as well as the only safe theory of the constitution whilst this principle shall guide my public conduct i consider it clear that under the war-making foreign invasion the constitution have confer upon congress power to declare war to raise and support army to provide and maintain a navy and to call forth the militia to repel invasion these high sovereign power necessarily involve important and responsible public duty and among they there be none so sacred and so imperative as that of preserve we soil from the invasion of a foreign enemy the constitution have therefore leave nothing on this point to construction but expressly require that the united state shall protect each of they -lrb- the state -rrb- against invasion now if a military road over we own territory be indispensably necessary to enable we to meet and repel the invader it follow as a necessary consequence not only that we possess the power but it be we imperative duty to construct such a road it would be a absurdity to invest a government with the unlimited power to make and conduct war and at the same time deny to it the only means of reach and defeat the enemy at the frontier without such a road it be quite evident we can not protect californium and we pacific possession against invasion we can not by any other means transport man and munitions of war from the atlantic state in sufficient time successfully to defend these remote and distant portion of the republic experience have prove that the route across the isthmus of central america be at best but a very uncertain and unreliable mode of communication but even if this be not the case they would at once be close against we in the event of war with a naval power so much stronger than we own as to enable it to blockade the port at either end of these route after all therefore we can only rely upon a military road through we own territory and ever since the origin of the government congress have be in the practice of appropriate money from the public treasury for the construction of such road the difficulty and the expense of construct a military railroad to connect we atlantic and pacific state have be greatly exaggerate the distance on the arizona route near the thirty-second parallel of north latitude between the western boundary of texa on the rio grande and the eastern boundary of californium on the colorado from the best exploration now within we knowledge do not exceed 470 mile and the face of the country be in the main favorable for obvious reason the government ought not to undertake the work itself by means of its own agent this ought to be commit to other agency which congress might assist either by grant of land or money or by both upon such term and condition as they may deem most beneficial for the country provision might thus be make not only for the safe rapid and economical transportation of troops and munitions of war but also of the public mail the commercial interest of the whole country both east and west would be greatly promote by such a road and above all it would be a powerful additional bond of union and although advantage of this kind whether postal commercial or political can not confer constitutional power yet they may furnish auxiliary argument in favor of expedite a work which in my judgment be clearly embrace within the war-making power for these reason i commend to the friendly consideration of congress the subject of the pacific railroad without finally commit myself to any particular route the report of the in practice already thirteen state and seven territory have be carve out of these land and still more than a thousand million of acre remain unsold what a boundless prospect this present to we country any people whilst i do not deny to congress the power when act _ bona fide _ as a proprietor to give away portion of they for the purpose of increase the value of the remainder yet consider the great temptation to abuse this power we can not be too cautious in its exercise actual settler under exist law be protect against other purchaser at the public sale in they right of preemption to the extent of a quarter section or 160 acre of land the remainder may then be dispose of at public or enter at private sale in unlimited quantity speculation have of late year prevail to a great extent in the public land the consequence have be that large portion of they have become the property of individual and company and thus the price be greatly enhance to those who desire to purchase for actual settlement in order to limit the area of speculation as much as possible the extinction of the indian title and the extension of the public survey ought only to keep pace with the tide of emigration if congress should hereafter grant alternate section to state or company as they have do heretofore i recommend that the intermediate section retain by the government should be subject to preemption by actual settler it ought ever to be we cardinal policy to reserve the public land as much as may be for actual settler and this at moderate price we shall thus not only best promote the prosperity of the new state and territory and the power of the union but shall secure home for we posterity for many generation the extension of we limit have bring within we jurisdiction many additional and populous tribe of indian a large proportion of which be wild untractable and difficult to control predatory and warlike in they disposition and habit it be impossible altogether to restrain they from commit aggression on each other as well as upon we frontier citizen and those emigrate to we distant state and territory hence expensive military expedition be frequently necessary to overawe and chastise the more lawless and hostile the present system of make they valuable present to influence they to remain at peace have prove ineffectual it be believe to be the better policy to colonize they in suitable locality where they can receive the rudiment of education and be gradually induce to adopt habit of industry so far as the experiment have be try it have work well in practice and it will doubtless prove to be less expensive than the present system the whole number of indian within we territorial limit be believe to be from the best datum in the interior department about 325000 not belong to he obedience to law and conformity to instruction be the best and safest guide for all officer civil and military and when they transcend these limit and act upon they own personal responsibility evil consequence almost inevitably follow under these circumstance when marshal rynder present himself at the state department on the 29th ultimo with general walker in custody the less determine than i have ever be to execute the neutrality law of the united state this be my imperative duty and i shall continue to perform it by all the means which the constitution and the law have place in my power my opinion of the value and importance of these law correspond entirely with that express by mr monroe in he message to congress of December 7 1819 that wise prudent and patriotic statesman say : it be of the highest importance to we national character and indispensable to the morality of we citizen that all violation of we neutrality should be prevent no door should be leave open for the evasion of we law no opportunity afford to any who may be dispose to take advantage of it to compromit the interest or the honor of the nation the crime of set on foot or provide the means for a military expedition within the united state to make war against a foreign state with which we be at peace be one of a aggravate and dangerous character and early engage the attention of congress whether the executive government possess any or what power under the constitution independently of congress to prevent or punish this and similar offens against the law of nation be a subject which engage the attention of we most eminent statesman in the time of the administration of general washington and on the occasion of the french revolution the act of congress of the 5th of June 1794 fortunately remove all the difficulty on this question which have theretofore exist the fifth and seventh section of this act which relate to the present question be the same in substance with the sixth and eighth section of the act of April 20 1818 and have now be in force for a period more than sixty year the military expedition render criminal by the act must have its origin must begin or be set on foot in the united state but the great object of the law be to save foreign state with whom we be at peace from the ravages of these lawless expedition proceed from we shore the seventh section alone therefore which simply define the crime and its punishment would have be inadequate to accomplish this purpose and enforce we international duty in order to render the law effectual it be necessary to prevent the carry on of such expedition to they consummation after they have succeed in leave we shore this have be do effectually and in clear and explicit language by the authority give to the president under the eighth section of the act to employ the land and naval force of the united state for the purpose of prevent the carry on of any such expedition or enterprise from the territory or jurisdiction of the united state against the territory or dominion of any foreign prince or state or of any colony district or people with whom the united state be at peace for these reason have commodore paulding intercept the steamer _ fashion _ with general walker and he command on board at any period before they enter the port of san juan de nicaragua and conduct they back to mobile this would have prevent they from carry on the expedition and have be not only a justifiable but a praiseworthy act the crime well deserve the punishment inflict upon it by we law it violate the principle of christianity morality and humanity hold sacred by all civilized nation and by none more than by the people of the united state disguise it as we may such a military expedition be a invitation to reckless and lawless man to enlist under the banner of any adventurer to rob plunder and murder the unoffending citizen of neighbor state who have never do they harm it be a usurpation of the war-making power which belong alone to congress and the government itself at least in the estimation of the world become a accomplice in the commission of this crime unless it adopt all the means necessary to prevent and to punish it it would be far better and more in accordance with the bold and manly character of we countryman for the government itself to get up such expedition than to allow they to proceed under the command of irresponsible adventurer we could then at least exercise some control over we own agent and prevent they from burn down city and commit other act of enormity of which we have read the avowed principle which lie at the foundation of the law of nation be contain in the divine command that all thing whatsoever ye would that man should do to you do ye even so to they try by this unerring rule we should be severely condemn if we shall not use we best exertion to arrest such expedition against we feeble sister republic of nicaragua one thing be very certain that a people never exist who would call any other nation to a stricter account than we should ourselves for tolerate lawless expedition from they shore to make war upon any portion of we territory by tolerate such expedition we shall soon lose the high character which we have enjoy ever since the day of washington for the faithful performance of we international obligation and duty and inspire distrust against we among the member of the great family of civilized nation but if motive of duty be not sufficient to restrain we from engage in such lawless enterprise we evident interest ought to dictate this policy these expedition be the most effectual mode of retard american progress although to promote this be the avowed object of the leader and contributor in such undertaking it be beyond question the destiny of we race to spread themselves over the continent of north america and this at no distant day should event be permit to take they natural course the tide of emigrant will flow to the south and nothing can eventually arrest its progress if permit to go there peacefully central america will soon contain a american population which will confer blessing and benefit as well upon the native as they respective government liberty under the restraint of law will preserve domestic peace whilst the different transit route across the isthmus in which we be so deeply interested will have assure protection nothing have retard this happy condition of affair so much as the unlawful expedition which have be fit out in the united state to make war upon the central american state have one-half the number of american citizen who have miserably perish in the first disastrous expedition of general walker settle in nicaragua as peaceful emigrant the object which we all desire would ere this have be in a great degree accomplish these expedition have cause the people of the central american state to regard we with dread and suspicion it be we true policy to remove this apprehension and to convince they that we intend to do they good and not evil we desire as the lead power on this continent to open and if need be to protect every transit route across the isthmus not only for we own benefit but that of the world and thus open a free access to central america and through it to we pacific possession this policy be commence under favorable auspices when the expedition under the command of general walker escape from we territory and proceed to punta arena should another expedition of a similar character again evade the vigilance of we officer and proceed to nicaragua this would be fatal at least for a season to the peaceful settlement of these country and to the policy of american progress the truth be that no
