expression of a hope that i would submit the same to the consideration of congress with the view of the admission of kansas into the union as a independent state in compliance with this request i herewith transmit to congress for they action the constitution of kansa with the ordinance respect the public land as well as the letter of mr calhoun date at lecompton on the 14th ultimo by which they be accompany have receive but a single copy of the constitution and ordinance i send this to the senate a great delusion seem to pervade the public mind in relation to the condition of party in kansa this arise from the difficulty of induce the american people to realize the fact that any portion of they should be in a state of rebellion against the government under which they live when we speak of the affair of kansas we be apt to refer merely to the existence of two violent political party in that territory divide on the question of slavery just as we speak of such party in the state this present no adequate idea of the true state of the case the divide line there be not between two political party both acknowledge the lawful existence of the government but between those who be loyal to this government and those who have endeavor to destroy its existence by force and by usurpation -- between those who sustain and those who have do all in they power to overthrow the territorial government establish by congress this government they would long since have subvert have it not be protect from they assault by the troops of the united state such have be the condition of affair since my inauguration ever since that period a large portion of the people of kansa have be in a state of rebellion against the government with a military leader at they head of a most turbulent and dangerous character they have never acknowledge but have constantly renounce and defy the government to which they owe allegiance and have be all the time in a state of resistance against its authority they have all the time be endeavor to subvert it and to establish a revolutionary government under the so-called topeka constitution in its stead even at this very moment the topeka legislature be in session whoever have read the correspondence of governor walker with the state department recently communicate to the senate will be convince that this picture be not overdrawn he always protest against the withdrawal of any portion of the military force of the united state from the territory deem its presence absolutely necessary for the preservation of the regular government and the execution of the law in he very first dispatch to the secretary of state date June 2 1857 he say : the most alarming movement however proceed from the assemble on the 9th June of the so-called topeka legislature with a view to the enactment of a entire code of law of course it will be my endeavor to prevent such a result as it would lead to inevitable and disastrous collision and in fact renew the civil war in kansa this be with difficulty prevent by the effort of governor walker but soon thereafter on the 14th of July we find he request general harney to furnish he a regiment of dragoon to proceed to the city of lawrence and this for the reason that he have receive authentic intelligence verify by he own actual observation that a dangerous rebellion have occur involve a open defiance of the law and the establishment of a insurgent government in that city in the governor 's dispatch of July 15 he inform the secretary of state that -- this movement at lawrence be the beginning of a plan originate in that city to organize insurrection throughout the territory and especially in all town city or county where the republican party have a majority lawrence be the hotb of all the abolition movement in this territory it be the town establish by the abolition society of the east and whilst there be respectable people there it be fill by a considerable number of mercenary who be pay by abolition society to perpetuate and diffuse agitation throughout kansa and prevent a peaceful settlement of this question have fail in induce they own so-called topeka state legislature to organize this insurrection lawrence have commence it herself and if not arrest the rebellion will extend throughout the territory and again : in order to send this communication immediately by mail i must close by assure you that the spirit of rebellion pervade the great mass of the republican party of this territory instigate as i entertain no doubt they be by eastern society have in view result most disastrous to the government and to the union and that the continue presence of general harney here be indispensable as originally stipulate by I with a large body of dragoon and several battery on the 20th July 1857 general lane under the authority of the topeka convention undertake as governor walker inform we -- to organize the whole so-called free-state party into volunteer and to take the name of all who refuse enrollment the profess object be to protect the poll at the election in August of the new insurgent topeka state legislature \* \* \* \* \* the object of take the name of all who refuse enrollment be to terrify the free-state conservative into submission this be prove by recent atrocity commit on such man by topekaite the speedy location of large body of regular troops here with two battery be necessary the lawrence insurgent await the development of this new revolutionary military organization in the governor 's dispatch of July 27 he say that general lane and he staff everywhere deny the authority of the territorial law and counsel a total disregard of these enactment without make further quotation of a similar character from other dispatch of governor walker it appear by a reference to mr stanton 's communication to general cass of the 9th of December last that the important step of call the legislature together be take after i -lrb- he -rrb- have become satisfied that the election order by the convention on the 21st instant could not be conduct without collision and bloodsh so intense be the disloyal feeling among the enemy of the government establish by congress that a election which afford they a opportunity if in the majority of make kansa a free state accord to they own profess desire could not be conduct without collision and bloodsh the truth be that up till the present moment the enemy of the exist government still adhere to they topeka revolutionary constitution and government the very first paragraph of the message of governor robinson date on the 7th of December to the topeka legislature now assemble at lawrence contain a open defiance of the constitution and law of the united state the governor say : the convention which frame the constitution at topeka originate with the people of kansas territory they have adopt and ratify the same twice by a direct vote and also indirectly through two election of state officer and member of the state legislature yet it have please the administration to regard the whole proceeding revolutionary this topeka government adhere to with such treasonable pertinacity be a government in direct opposition to the existing government prescribe and recognize by congress it be a usurpation of the same character as it would be for a portion of the people of any state of the union to undertake to establish a separate government within its limit for the purpose of redress any grievance real or imaginary of which they might complain against the legitimate state government such a principle if carry into execution would destroy all lawful authority and produce universal anarchy from this statement of fact the reason become palpable why the enemy of the government authorize by congress have refuse to vote for delegate to the kansas constitutional convention and also afterwards on the question of slavery submit by it to the people it be because they have ever refuse to sanction or recognize any other constitution than that frame at topeka have the whole lecompton constitution be submit to the people the adherent of this organization would doubtless have vote against it because if successful they would thus have remove a obstacle out of the way of they own revolutionary constitution they would have do this not upon a consideration of the merit of the whole or any part of the lecompton constitution but simply because they have ever resist the authority of the government authorize by congress from which it emanate such be the unfortunate condition of affair in the territory what be the right as well as the duty of the law-abiding people be they silently and patiently to submit to the topeka usurpation or adopt the necessary measure to establish a constitution under the authority of the organic law of congress that this law recognize the right of the people of the territory without any enable act from congress to form a state constitution be too clear for argument for congress to leave the people of the territory perfectly free in frame they constitution to form and regulate they domestic institution in they own way subject only to the constitution of the united state and then to say that they shall not be permit to proceed and frame a constitution in they own way without a express authority from congress appear to be almost a contradiction in term it would be much more plausible to contend that congress have no power to pass such a enable act than to argue that the people of a territory might be keep out of the union for a indefinite period and until it might please congress to permit they to exercise the right of self-government this would be to adopt not they own way but the way which congress might prescribe it be impossible that any people could have proceed with more regularity in the formation of a constitution than the people of kansa have do it be necessary first to ascertain whether it be the desire of the people to be relieve from they territorial dependence and establish a state government for this purpose the territorial legislature in 1855 pass a law for take the sense of the people of this territory upon the expediency of call a convention to form a state constitution at the general election to be hold in October 1856 the sense of the people be accordingly take and they decide in favor of a convention it be true that at this election the enemy of the territorial government do not vote because they be then engage at topeka without the slightest pretext of lawful authority in frame a constitution of they own for the purpose of subvert the territorial government in pursuance of this decision of the people in favor of a convention the territorial legislature on the 27th day of February 1857 pass a act for the election of delegate on the third Monday of June 1857 to frame a state constitution this law be as fair in its provision as any that ever pass a legislative body for a similar purpose the right of suffrage at this election be clearly and justly define every _ bona fide _ inhabitant of the territory of kansa on the third Monday of June the day of the election who be a citizen of the united state above the age of 21 and have reside therein for three month previous to that date be entitle to vote in order to avoid all interference from neighbor state or territory with the freedom and fairness of the election provision be make for the registry of the qualify voter and in pursuance thereof 9251 voter be register governor walker do he whole duty in urge all the qualify citizen of kansa to vote at this election in he inaugural address on the 27th may last he inform they that -- under we practice the preliminary act of frame a state constitution be uniformly perform through the instrumentality of a convention of delegate choose by the people themselves that convention be now about to be elect by you under the call of the territorial legislature create and still recognize by the authority of congress and clothe by it in the comprehensive language of the organic law with full power to make such a enactment the territorial legislature then in assemble this convention be fully sustain by the act of congress and the authority of the convention be distinctly recognize in my instruction from the president of the united state the governor also clearly and distinctly warn they what would be the consequence if they should not participate in the election the people of kansas then -lrb- he say -rrb- be invite by the highest authority know to the constitution to participate freely and fairly in the election of delegate to frame a constitution and state government the law have perform its entire appropriate function when it extend to the people the right of suffrage but it can not compel the performance of that duty throughout we whole union however and wherever free government prevail those who abstain from the exercise of the right of suffrage authorize those who do vote to act for they in that contingency and the absentee be as much bind under the law and constitution where there be no fraud or violence by the act of the majority of those who do vote as if all have participate in the election otherwise as voting must be voluntary self-government would be impracticable and monarchy or despotism would remain as the only alternative it may also be observe that at this period any hope if such have exist that the topeka constitution would ever be recognize by congress must have be abandon congress have adjourn on the 3d march previous have recognize the legal existence of the territorial legislature in a variety of form which i need not enumerate indeed the delegate elect to the house of representative under a territorial law have be admit to he seat and have just complete he term of service on the day previous to my inauguration this be the propitious moment for settle all difficulty in kansa this be the time for abandon the revolutionary topeka organization and for the enemy of the exist government to conform to the law and to unite with its friend in frame a state constitution but this they refuse to do and the consequence of they refusal to submit to lawful authority and vote at the election of delegate may yet prove to be of a most deplorable character would that the respect for the law of the land which so eminently distinguish the man of the past generation could be revive it be a disregard and violation of law which have for year keep the territory of kansa in a state of almost open rebellion against its government it be the same spirit which have produce actual rebellion in utah we only safety consist in obedience and conformity to law should a general spirit against its enforcement prevail this will prove fatal to we as a nation we acknowledge no master but the law and should we cut loose from its restraint and everyone do what seemeth good in he own eye we case will indeed be hopeless the enemy of the territorial government determine still to resist the authority of congress they refuse to vote for delegate to the convention not because from circumstance which i need not detail there be a omission to register the comparatively few voter who be inhabitant of certain county of kansa in the early spring of 1857 but because they have predetermine at all hazard to adhere to they revolutionary organization and defeat the establishment of any other constitution than that which they have frame at topeka the election be therefore suffer to pass by default but of this result the qualify elector who refuse to vote can never justly complain from this review it be manifest that the lecompton convention accord to every principle of constitutional law be legally constitute and be invest with power to frame a constitution the sacred principle of popular sovereignty have be invoke in favor of the enemy of law and order in kansa but in what manner be popular sovereignty to be exercise in this country if not through the instrumentality of established law in certain small republic of ancient time the people do assemble in primary meeting pass law and direct public affair in we country this be manifestly impossible popular sovereignty can be exercise here only through the ballot box and if the people will refuse to exercise it in this manner as they have do in kansa at the election of delegate it be not for they to complain that they rights have be violate the kansa convention thus lawfully constitute proceed to frame a constitution and have complete they work finally adjourn on the 7th day of November last they do not think proper to submit the whole of this constitution to a popular vote but they do submit the question whether kansa should be a free or a slave state to the people this be the question which have convulse the union and shake it to its very center this be the question which have light up the flame of civil war in kansa and have produce dangerous sectional party throughout the confederacy it be of a character so paramount in respect to the condition of kansas as to rivet the anxious attention of the people of the whole country upon it and it alone no person thought of any other question for my own part when i instruct governor walker in general term in favor of submit the constitution to the people i have no object in view except the all-absorbing question of slavery in what manner the people of kansa might regulate they other concern be not a subject which attract any attention in fact the general provision of we recent state constitution after a experience of eight year be so similar and so excellent that it would be difficult to go far wrong at the present day in frame a new constitution i then believe and still believe that under the organic act the kansa convention be bind to submit this all-important question of slavery to the people it be never however my opinion that independently of this act they would have be bind to submit any portion of the constitution to a popular vote in order to give it validity have i entertain such a opinion this would have be in opposition to many precedent in we history commence in the very best age of the republic it would have be in opposition to the principle which pervade we institution and which be every day carry out into practice that the people have the right to delegate to representative choose by themselves they sovereign power to frame constitution enact law and perform many other important act without require that these should be subject to they subsequent approbation it would be a most inconvenient limitation of they own power impose by the people upon themselves to exclude they from exercise they sovereignty in any lawful manner they think proper it be true that the people of kansa might if they have please have require the convention to submit the constitution to a popular vote but this they have not do the only remedy therefore in this case be that which exist in all other similar case if the delegate who frame the kansa constitution have in any manner violate the will of they constituent the people always possess the power to change they constitution or they law accord to they own pleasure the question of slavery be submit to a election of the people of kansa on the 21st December last in obedience to the mandate of the constitution here again a fair opportunity be present to the adherent of the topeka constitution if they be the majority to decide this exciting question in they own way and thus restore peace to the distract territory but they again refuse to exercise they right of popular sovereignty and again suffer the election to pass by default i heartily rejoice that a wiser and better spirit prevail among a large majority of these people on the first Monday of January and that they do on that day vote under the lecompton constitution for a governor and other state officer a member of congress and for member of the legislature this election be warmly contest by the party and a larger vote be poll than at any previous election in the territory we may now reasonably hope that the revolutionary topeka organization will be speedily and finally abandon and this will go far toward the final settlement of the unhappy difference in kansas if fraud have be commit at this election either by one or both party the legislature and the people of kansas under they constitution will know how to redress themselves and punish these detestable but too common crime without any outside interference the people of kansa have then in they own way and in strict accordance with the organic act frame a constitution and state government have submit the all-important question of slavery to the people and have elect a governor a member to represent they in congress member of the state legislature and other state officer they now ask admission into the union under this constitution which be republican in its form it be for congress to decide whether they will admit or reject the state which have thus be create for my own part i be decidedly in favor of its admission and thus terminate the kansa question this will carry out the great principle of nonintervention recognize and sanction by the organic act which declare in express language in favor of nonintervention by congress with slavery in the state or territory leave the people thereof perfectly free to form and regulate they domestic institution in they own way subject only to the constitution of the united state in this manner by localize the question of slavery and confine it to the people whom it immediately concern every patriot anxiously expect that this question would be banish from the hall of congress where it have always exert a baneful influence throughout the whole country it be proper that i should briefly refer to the election hold under a act of the territorial legislature on the first Monday of January last on the lecompton constitution this election be hold after the territory have be prepare for admission into the union as a sovereign state and when no authority exist in the territorial legislature which could possibly destroy its existence or change its character the election which be peaceably conduct under my instruction involve a strange inconsistency a large majority of the person who vote against the lecompton constitution be at the very same time and place recognize its valid existence in the most solemn and authentic manner by vote under its provision i have yet receive no official information of the result of this election as a question of expediency after the right have be maintain it may be wise to reflect upon the benefit to kansa and to the whole country which would result from its immediate admission into the union as well as the disaster which may follow its rejection domestic peace will be the happy consequence of its admission and that fine territory which have hitherto be tear by dissension will rapidly increase in population and wealth and speedily realize the blessing and the comfort which follow in the train of agricultural and mechanical industry the people will then be sovereign and can regulate they own affair in they own way if a majority of they desire to abolish domestic slavery within the state there be no other possible mode by which this can be effect so speedily as by prompt admission the will of the majority be supreme and irresistible when express in a orderly and lawful manner they can make and unmake constitution at pleasure it would be absurd to say that they can impose fetter upon they own power which they can not afterwards remove if they could do this they might tie they own hand for a hundred as well as for ten year these be fundamental principle of american freedom and be recognize i believe in some form or other by every state constitution and if congress in the act of admission should think proper to recognize they i can perceive no objection to such a course this have be do emphatically in the constitution of kansas it declare in the bill of rights that all political power be inherent in the people and all free government be found on they authority and institute for they benefit and therefore they have at all time a inalienable and indefeasible right to alter reform or abolish they form of government in such manner as they may think proper the great state of new york be at this moment govern under a constitution frame and establish in direct opposition to the mode prescribe by the previous constitution if therefore the provision change the kansa constitution after the year 1864 could by possibility be construe into a prohibition to make such a change previous to that period this prohibition would be wholly unavailing the legislature already elect may at its very first session submit the question to a vote of the people whether they will or will not have a convention to amend they constitution and adopt all necessary means for give effect to the popular will it have be solemnly adjudge by the highest judicial tribunal know to we law that slavery exist in kansa by virtue of the constitution of the united state kansa be therefore at this moment as much a slave state as georgium or south carolina without this the equality of the sovereign state compose the union would be violate and the use and enjoyment of a territory acquire by the common treasure of all the state would be close against the people and the property of nearly half the member of the confederacy slavery can therefore never be prohibit in kansas except by means of a constitutional provision and in no other manner can this be obtain so promptly if a majority of the people desire it as by admit it into the union under its present constitution on the other hand should congress reject the constitution under the idea of afford the disaffected in kansas a third opportunity of prohibit slavery in the state which they might have do twice before if in the majority no man can foretell the consequence if congress for the sake of those man who refuse to vote for delegate to the convention when they might have exclude slavery from the constitution and who afterwards refuse to vote on the 21st December last when they might as they claim have stricken slavery from the constitution should now reject the state because slavery remain in the constitution it be manifest that the agitation upon this dangerous subject will be renew in a more alarming form than it have ever yet assume every patriot in the country have indulge the hope that the kansa and nebraska act would put a final end to the slavery agitation at least in congress which have for more than twenty year convulse the country and endanger the union this act involve great and fundamental principle and if fairly carry into effect will settle the question should the agitation be again revive should the people of the sister state be again estrange from each other with more than they former bitterness this will arise from a cause so far as the interest of kansa be concern more trifling and insignificant than have ever stir the element of a great people into commotion to the people of kansas the only practical difference between admission or rejection depend simply upon the fact whether they can themselves more speedily change the present constitution if it do not accord with the will of the majority or frame a second constitution to be submit to congress hereafter even if this be a question of mere expediency and not of right the small difference of time one way or the other be of not the least importance when contrast with the evil which must necessarily result to the whole country from a revival of the slavery agitation in consider this question it should never be forget that in proportion to its insignificance let the decision be what it may so far as it may affect the few thousand inhabitant of kansa who have from the beginning resist the constitution and the law for this very reason the rejection of the constitution will be so much the more keenly feel by the people of fourteen of the state of this union where slavery be recognize under the constitution of the united state again the speedy admission of kansas into the union would restore peace and quiet to the whole country already the affair of this territory have engross a undue proportion of public attention they have sadly affect the friendly relation of the people of the state with each other and alarm the fear of patriot for the safety of the union kansa once admit into the union the excitement become localized and will soon die away for want of outside aliment then every difficulty will be settle at the ballot box besides -- and this be no trifling consideration -- i shall then be enable to withdraw the troops of the united state from kansa and employ they on branch of service where they be much need they have be keep there on the earnest importunity of governor walker to maintain the existence of the territorial government and secure the execution of the law he consider that at least 2000 regular troops under the command of general harney be necessary for this purpose act upon he reliable information i have be oblige in some degree to interfere with the expedition to utah in order to keep down rebellion in kansa this have involve a very heavy expense to the government kansa once admit it be believe there will no longer be any occasion there for troops of the united state i have thus perform my duty on this important question under a deep sense of responsibility to god and my country my public life will terminate within a brief period and i have no other object of earthly ambition than to leave my country in a peaceful and prosperous condition and to live in the affection and respect of my countryman the dark and ominous cloud which now appear to be impend over the union i conscientiously believe may be dissipate with honor to every portion of it by the admission of kansas during the present session of congress whereas if she should be reject i greatly fear these cloud will become darker and more ominous than any which have ever yet threaten the constitution and the union jame buchanan _ to the of January this sum the secretary say do not include such amount as may be appropriate by congress over and above the estimate submit to they by the department and i have no datum on which to estimate and the 1st of January would amount to $ 25000000 leave a deficit of $ 15000000 inclusive of the sum of about $ 3000000 the least amount require to be in the treasury at all time to secure its as might be make by congress over and above these estimate there be embrace in this sum of $ 15000000 estimate to the amount of about $ 1750000 for the three volunteer regiment authorize by the act of July and the 1st January next can not be ascertain until the appropriation bill as well as the private bill contain appropriation shall have finally pass adversity teach useful lesson to nation as well as individual the habit of extravagant expenditure foster by a large surplus in the treasury must now be correct or the country will be involve in serious financial difficulty under any form of government extravagance in expenditure must be the natural consequence when those who authorize the expenditure feel no responsibility in provide the means of payment such have be for a number of year we condition previously to the late monetary revulsion in the country fortunately at least for the cause of public economy the case be now reverse and to the extent of the appropriation whatever these the session i state in the annual message to congress of December last that -- from the practice of congress such a examination of each bill as the constitution require have be render impossible the most important business of each session be generally crowd into its last hour and the alternative present to the president be either to violate the constitutional duty which he owe to the people and approve bill which for want of time it be impossible he should have examine or by he refusal to do this subject the country and individual to great loss and inconvenience \* \* \* \* \* for my own part i have deliberately determine that i shall approve no bill which i have not examine and it will be a case of extreme and most urgent necessity which shall ever induce I to depart from this rule the present condition of the treasury absolutely require that i should adhere to this resolution on the present occasion for the reason which i have heretofore present in former time it be believe to be the true character of a appropriation bill simply to carry into effect exist law and the established policy of the country a practice have however grow up of late year to ingraft on such bill at the last hour of the session large appropriation for new and important object not provide for by preexist law and when no time be leave to the executive for they examination and investigation no alternative be thus leave to the president but either to approve measure without examination or by veto a appropriation bill seriously to embarrass the operation of the government this practice could never have prevail without a surplus in the treasury sufficiently large to cover a indefinite amount of appropriation necessity now compel we to arrest it at least so far as to afford time to ascertain the amount appropriate and to provide the means of its payment for all these reason i recommend to congress to postpone the day of adjournment for a brief period i promise that not a hour shall be lose in ascertain the amount of appropriation make by they for which it will be necessary to provide i know it will be inconvenient for the member to attend a call session and this above all of america a proclamation whereas the territory of utah be settle by certain emigrant from the state and from foreign country who have for several year past manifest a spirit of insubordination to the constitution and law of the united state the great mass of those settler act under the influence of leader to whom they seem to have surrender they judgment refuse to be control by any other authority they have be often advise to obedience and these friendly counsel have be answer with defiance the officer of the federal government have be drive from the territory for no offense but a effort to do they swear duty other have be prevent from go there by threat of assassination judge have be violently interrupt in the performance of they function and the record of the court have be seize and destroy or conceal many other act of unlawful violence have be perpetrate and the right to repeat they have be openly claim by the lead inhabitant with at least the silent acquiescence of nearly all the other they hostility to the lawful government of the country have at length become so violent that no officer bear a commission from the chief magistrate of the union can enter the territory or remain there with safety and all those officer recently appoint have be unable to go to salt lake or anywhere else in utah beyond the immediate power of the army indeed such be believe to be the condition to which a strange system of terrorism have bring the inhabitant of that region that no one among they could express a opinion favorable to this government or even propose to obey its law without expose he life and property to peril after carefully consider this state of affair and maturely weigh the obligation i be under to see the law faithfully execute it seem to I right and proper that i should make such use of the military force at my disposal as might be necessary to protect the federal officer in go into the territory of utah and in perform they duty after arrive there i accordingly order a detachment of the army to march for the city of salt lake or within reach of that place and to act in case of need as a posse for the enforcement of the law but in the meantime the hatred of that misguided people for the just and legal authority of the government have become so intense that they resolve to measure they military strength with that of the union they have organize a armed force far from contemptible in point of number and train it if not with skill at least with great assiduity and perseverance while the troops of the united state be on they march a train of baggage wagon which happen to be unprotected be attack and destroy by a portion of the mormon force and the provision and store with which the train be laden be wantonly burn in short they present attitude be one of decide and unreserved enmity to the united state and to all they loyal citizen they determination to oppose the authority of the government by military force have not only be express in word but manifest in overt act of the most unequivocal character fellow-citizen of utah this be rebellion against the government to which you owe allegiance it be levy war against the united state and involve you in the guilt of treason persistence in it will bring you to condign punishment to ruin and to shame for it be mere madness to suppose that with you limited resource you can successfully resist the force of this great and powerful nation if you have calculate upon the forbearance of the united state if you have permit yourselve to suppose that this government will fail to put forth its strength and bring you to submission you have fall into a grave mistake you have settle upon territory which lie geographically in the heart of the union the land you live upon be purchase by the united state and pay for out of they treasury the proprietary right and title to it be in they and not in you utah be bound on every side by state and territory whose people be true to the union it be absurd to believe that they will or can permit you to erect in they very midst a government of you own not only independent of the authority which they all acknowledge but hostile to they and they interest do not deceive yourselve nor try to mislead other by propagate the idea that this be a crusade against you religion the constitution and law of this country can take no notice of you creed whether it be true or false that be a question between you god and yourselve in which i disclaim all right to interfere if you obey the law keep the peace and respect the just rights of other you will be perfectly secure and may live on in you present faith or change it for another at you pleasure every intelligent man among you know very well that this government have never directly or indirectly seek to molest you in you worship to control you in you ecclesiastical affair or even to influence you in you religious opinion this rebellion be not merely a violation of you legal duty it be without just cause without reason without excuse you never make a complaint that be not listen to with patience you never exhibit a real grievance that be not redress as promptly as it could be the law and regulation enact for you government by congress have be equal and just and they enforcement be manifestly necessary for you own welfare and happiness you have never ask they repeal they be similar in every material respect to the law which have be pass for the other territory of the union and which everywhere else -lrb- with one partial exception -rrb- have be cheerfully obey no people ever live who be freer from unnecessary legal restraint than you human wisdom never devise a political system which bestow more blessing or impose lighter burden than the government of the united state in its operation upon the territory but be anxious to save the effusion of blood and to avoid the indiscriminate punishment of a whole people for crime of which it be not probable that all be equally guilty i offer now a free and full pardon to all who will submit themselves to the just authority of the federal government if you refuse to accept it let the consequence fall upon you own head but i conjure you to pause deliberately and reflect well before you reject this tender of peace and good will now therefore i james buchanan president of the united state have think proper to issue this my proclamation enjoin upon all public officer in the territory of utah to be diligent and faithful to the full extent of they power in the execution of the law command all citizen of the united state in say territory to aid and assist the officer in the performance of they duty offer to the inhabitant of utah who shall submit to the law a free pardon for the sedition and treason heretofore by they committed warn those who shall persist after notice of this proclamation in the present rebellion against the united state that they must expect no further lenity but look to be rigorously deal with accord to they desert and declare that the military force now in utah and hereafter to be send there will not be withdraw until the inhabitant of that territory shall manifest a proper sense of the duty which they owe to this government -lrb- seal -rrb- in testimony whereof i have hereunto set my hand and cause the seal of the united state to be affix to these connect therewith as i have reason to believe have issue and sell bond and other contract pledge the public land of nicaragua and the transit route through its territory as a security for they secretary of state _ second annual message washington city _ December 6 1858 _ _ fellow-citizen of the senate and house of representative _ : when we compare the condition of the country at the present day with what it be one year ago at the meeting of congress we have much reason for gratitude to that almighty providence which have never fail to interpose for we relief at the most critical period of we history one year ago the sectional strife between the north and the south on the dangerous subject of slavery have again become so intense as to threaten the peace and perpetuity of the confederacy the application for the admission of kansas as a state into the union foster this unhappy agitation and bring the whole subject once more before congress it be the desire of every patriot that such measure of legislation might be adopt as would remove the excitement from the state and confine it to the territory where it legitimately belong much have be do i be happy to say toward the accomplishment of this object during the last session of congress the supreme court of the united state have previously decide that all american citizen have a equal right to take into the territory whatever be hold as property under the law of any of the state and to hold such property there under the guardianship of the federal constitution so long as the territorial condition shall remain this be now a well-established position and the proceedings of the last session be alone want to give it practical effect the principle have be recognize in some form or other by a almost unanimous vote of both house of congress that a territory have a right to come into the union either as a free or a slave state accord to the will of a majority of its people the just equality of all the state have thus be vindicate and a fruitful source of dangerous dissension among they have be remove whilst such have be the beneficial tendency of you legislative proceedings outside of kansas they influence have nowhere be so happy as within that territory itself leave to manage and control its own affair in its own way without the pressure of external influence the revolutionary topeka organization and all resistance to the territorial government establish by congress have be finally abandon as a natural consequence that fine territory now appear to be tranquil and prosperous and be attract increase thousand of immigrant to make it they happy home the past unfortunate experience of kansa have enforce the lesson so often already teach that resistance to lawful authority under we form of government can not fail in the end to prove disastrous to its author have the people of the territory yield obedience to the law enact by they legislature it would at the present moment have contain a large additional population of industrious and enterprising citizen who have be deter from enter its border by the existence of civil strife and organize rebellion it be the resistance to rightful authority and the persevere attempt to establish a revolutionary government under the topeka constitution which cause the people of kansa to commit the grave error of refuse to vote for delegate to the convention to frame a constitution under a law not deny to be fair and just in its provision this refusal to vote be the prolific source of all the evil which have follow in they hostility to the territorial government they disregard the principle absolutely essential to the working of we form of government that a majority of those who vote not the majority who may remain at home from whatever cause must decide the result of a election for this reason seek to take advantage of they own error they deny the authority of the convention thus elect to frame a constitution the convention notwithstanding proceed to adopt a constitution unexceptionable in its general feature and provide for the submission of the slavery question to a vote of the people which in my opinion they be bind to do under the kansa and nebraska act this be the all-important question which have alone convulse the territory and yet the opponent of the lawful government persist in they first error refrain from exercise they right to vote and prefer that slavery should continue rather than surrender they revolutionary topeka organization a wiser and better spirit seem to prevail before the first Monday of January last when a election be hold under the constitution a majority of the people then vote for a governor and other state officer for a member of congress and member of the state legislature this election be warmly contest by the two political party in kansa and a greater vote be poll than at any previous election a large majority of the member of the legislature elect belong to that party which have previously refuse to vote the antislavery party be thus place in the ascendant and the political power of the state be in they own hand have congress admit kansa into the union under the lecompton constitution the legislature might at its very first session have submit the question to a vote of the people whether they would or would not have a convention to amend they constitution either on the slavery or any other question and have adopt all necessary means for give speedy effect to the will of the majority thus the kansa question would have be immediately and finally settle under these circumstance i submit to congress the constitution thus frame with all the officer already elect necessary to put the state government into operation accompany by a strong recommendation in favor of the admission of kansas as a state in the course of my long public life i have never perform any official act which in the retrospect have afford I more heartfelt satisfaction its admission could have inflict no possible injury on any human be whilst it would within a brief period have restore peace to kansa and harmony to the union in that event the slavery question would ere this have be finally settle accord to the legally express will of a majority of the voter and popular sovereignty would thus have be vindicate in a constitutional manner with my deep conviction of duty i could have pursue no other course it be true that as a individual i have express a opinion both before and during the session of the convention in favor of submit the remain clause of the constitution as well as that concern slavery to the people but act in a official character neither myself nor any human authority have the power to rejudge the proceedings of the convention and declare the constitution which it have frame to be a nullity to have do this would have be a violation of the kansa and nebraska act which leave the people of the territory perfectly free to form and regulate they domestic institution in they own way subject only to the constitution of the united state it would equally have violate the great principle of popular sovereignty at the foundation of we institution to deprive the people of the power if they think proper to exercise it of confide to delegate elect by themselves the trust of frame a constitution without require they to subject they constituent to the trouble expense and delay of a second election it would have be in opposition to many precedent in we history commence in the very best age of the republic of the admission of territory as state into the union without a previous vote of the people approve they constitution it be to be lament that a question so insignificant when view in its practical effect on the people of kansas whether decide one way or the other should have kindle such a flame of excitement throughout the country this reflection may prove to be a lesson of wisdom and of warn for we future guidance white inhabitant large band of hostile and predatory indian roam promiscuously over the mexican state of chihuahua and sonora and we adjoining territory the local government of these state be on we remote settler a state of anarchy and violence prevail throughout that distant frontier the law be a dead letter and life and property wholly insecure for this reason the settlement of arizona be arrest whilst it be of great importance that a chain of inhabitant should extend all along its southern border sufficient for they own protection and that of the united state mail pass to and from within the same and this i earnestly recommend to congress this protection may be withdraw as soon as local government shall be establish in these mexican state capable of perform they duty to the prove equally effectual for the protection of they citizen on that remote and lawless frontier as for citizen of the united state and in this connection permit I to recall you attention to the condition of arizona the population of that territory numbering as be allege more than 10000 soul be practically without a government without law and without any regular administration of justice murder and other crime be commit with impunity this state of thing call loudly for redress and i therefore repeat my recommendation for the establishment of a territorial government over arizona the political condition of the narrow isthmus of central america through which transit route pass between the atlantic and pacific ocean present a subject of deep interest to all commercial nation it be over these transit that a large proportion of the trade and travel between the european and asiatic continent be destine to pass to the united state these route be of incalculable importance as a means of communication between they atlantic and pacific possession the latter now extend throughout seventeen degree of latitude on the pacific coast embrace the important state of californium and the flourishing territory of oregon and washington all commercial nation therefore have a deep and direct interest that these communication shall be render secure from interruption if a arm of the sea connect the two ocean penetrate through nicaragua and costa rica it could not be pretend that these state would have the right to arrest or retard its navigation to the injury of other nation the transit by land over this narrow isthmus occupy nearly the same position it be a highway in which they themselves have little interest when compare with the vast interest of the rest of the world whilst they rights of sovereignty ought to be respect it be the duty of other nation to require that this important passage shall not be interrupt by the civil war and revolutionary outbreak which have so frequently occur in that region the stake be too important to be leave at the mercy of rival company claim to hold conflict contract with nicaragua the commerce of other nation be not to stand still and await the adjustment of such petty controversy the government of the united state expect no more than this and they will not be satisfy with less they would not if they could derive any advantage from the nicaragua transit not common to the rest of the world its neutrality and protection for the common use of all nation be they only object they have no objection that nicaragua shall demand and receive a fair compensation from the company and individual who may traverse the route but they insist that it shall never hereafter be close by a arbitrary decree of that government if dispute arise between it and those with whom they may have enter into contract these must be adjust by some fair tribunal provide for the purpose and the route must not be close pend the controversy this be we whole policy and it can not fail to be acceptable to other nation all these difficulty might be avoid if consistently with the good faith of nicaragua the use of this transit could be throw open to general competition provide at the same time for the payment of a reasonable rate to the nicaraguan government on passenger and freight in August 1852 the accessory transit company make its first inter-oceanic trip over the nicaraguan route and continue in successful operation with great advantage to the public until the 18th February 1856 when it be close and the grant to this company as well as its charter be summarily and arbitrarily revoke by the government of president riva previous to this date however in 1854 serious dispute concern the settlement of they account have arise between the company and the government threaten the interruption of the route at any moment these the unite state in vain endeavor to compose it would be useless to narrate the various proceedings which take place between the party up till the time when the transit be discontinue suffice it to say that since February 1856 it have remain closed greatly to the prejudice of citizen of the united state since that time the competition have cease between the rival route of panama and nicaragua and in consequence thereof a unjust and unreasonable amount have be exact from we citizen for they passage to and from california a treaty be sign on the 16th day of November 1857 by the secretary of state and minister of nicaragua under the stipulation of which the use and protection of the transit route would have be secure not only to the united state but equally to all other nation how and on what pretext this treaty have fail to receive the ratification of the nicaraguan government will appear by the papers herewith communicate from the state department the principal objection seem to have be to the provision authorize the united state to employ force to keep the route open in case nicaragua should fail to perform she duty in this respect from the feebleness of that republic its frequent change of government and its constant internal dissension this have become a most important stipulation and one essentially necessary not only for the security of the route but for the safety of american citizen pass and repass to and from we pacific possession be such a stipulation embrace in a treaty between the united state and nicaragua the knowledge of this fact would of itself most probably prevent hostile party from commit aggression on the route and render we actual interference for its protection unnecessary the executive government of this country in its intercourse with foreign nation be limit to the employment of diplomacy alone when this fail it can proceed no further it can not legitimately resort to force without the direct authority of congress except in resist and repel hostile attack it would have no authority to enter the territory of nicaragua even to prevent the destruction of the transit and protect the life and property of we own citizen on they passage it be true that on a sudden emergency of this character the president would direct any armed force in the vicinity to march to they relief but in do this he would act upon he own responsibility under these circumstance i earnestly recommend to congress the passage of a act authorize the president under such restriction as they may deem proper to employ the land and naval force of the united state in prevent the transit from be obstruct or close by lawless violence and in protect the life and property of american citizen travel thereupon require at the same time that these force shall be withdraw the moment the danger shall have pass away without such a provision we citizen will be constantly expose to interruption in they progress and to lawless violence a similar necessity exist for the passage of such a act for the protection of the panama and tehuantepec route in reference to the panama route the united state by they exist treaty with new granada expressly guarantee the neutrality of the isthmus with the view that the free transit from the one to the other sea may not be interrupted or embarrassed in any future time while this treaty exist in regard to the tehuantepec route which have be recently open under the most favorable auspices we treaty with mexico of the 30th December 1853 secure to the citizen of the united state a right of transit over it for they person and merchandise and stipulate that neither government shall interpose any obstacle thereto it also concede to the united state the right to transport across the isthmus in closed bag the mail of the united state not intend for distribution along the line of the communication also the effect of the united state government and its citizen which may be intend for transit and not for distribution on the isthmus free of custom-house or other charge by the mexican government these treaty stipulation with new granada and mexico in addition to the consideration applicable to the nicaragua route seem to require legislation for the purpose of carry they into effect recently be make to collect these tax nor be any anticipate under present circumstance with the empire of brazil we relation be of the most friendly character the production of the two country and especially those of a agricultural nature be such as to invite extensive mutual exchange a large quantity of american flour be consume in brazil whilst more than treble the amount in value of brazilian coffee be consume in the united state whilst this be the case a heavy duty have be levy until very recently upon the importation of american flour into brazil i be gratified however to be however that it may not be find necessary to resort to this last alternative when congress meet in December last the business of the country have just be crush by one of those periodical revulsion which be the inevitable consequence of we unsound and extravagant system of bank credit and inflated currency with all the element of national wealth in abundance we manufacture be suspend we useful public and private enterprise be arrest and thousand of laborer be deprive of employment and reduce to want universal distress prevail among the commercial manufacturing and mechanical class this revulsion be feel the more severely in the united state because similar cause have produce the like deplorable effect throughout the commercial nation of europe all be experience sad reverse at the same moment we manufacturer everywhere suffer severely not because of the recent reduction in the tariff of duty on import but because there be no demand at any price for they production the people be oblige to restrict themselves in they purchase to article of prime necessity in the general prostration of business the iron manufacturer in different state probably suffer more than any other class a much higher standard the tariff of 1857 have no agency in the result the general cause exist throughout the world could not have be control by the legislation of any particular country the periodical revulsion which have exist in we past history must continue to return at interval so long as we present unbounded system of bank credit shall prevail they will however probably be the less severe in future because it be not to be expect at least for many year to come that the commercial nation of europe with whose interest we own be so materially involve will expose themselves to similar calamity but this subject be treat so much at large in my last annual message that i shall not now pursue it further still i respectfully renew the recommendation in favor of the passage of a uniform bankrupt law applicable to banking institution this be all the direct power over the subject which i believe the federal government possess such a law would mitigate though it might not prevent the evil the instinct of self-preservation might produce a wholesome restraint upon they banking business if they know in advance that a suspension of specie payment would inevitably produce they civil death but the effect of the revulsion be now slowly but surely pass away the energy and enterprise of we citizen with we unbounded resource will within the period of another year restore a with we own must ever produce disastrous result to we domestic manufacture no tariff short of absolute prohibition can prevent these evil consequence in connection with this subject it be proper to refer to we financial condition the same cause which have produce pecuniary distress throughout the country have so reduce the amount of import from foreign country that the revenue have prove inadequate to meet the necessary expense of the government to supply the deficiency congress by the act of December 23 1857 authorize the issue of $ 20000000 of treasury note and this prove inadequate the ordinary expense of the government this would be a most ruinous policy in case of war we credit must be we chief resource at least for the first year and this would be greatly impair by have contract a large debt in time of peace it be we true policy to increase we revenue so as to equal we expenditure it would be ruinous to continue to borrow besides it may be proper to observe that the incidental protection thus afford by a revenue tariff would at the present moment to some extent increase the confidence of the manufacturing interest and give a fresh impulse to we revive business to this surely no person will object in regard to the mode of assess and collect duty under a strictly revenue tariff i have long entertain and often express the opinion that sound policy require this should be do by specific duty in case to which these can be properly apply they be well adapt to commodity which be usually sell by weight or by measure and which from they nature be of equal or of nearly equal value such for example be the article of iron of different class raw sugar and foreign wine and spirit in my deliberate judgment specific duty be the best if not the only means of secure the revenue against false and fraudulent invoice and such have be the practice adopt for this purpose by other commercial nation besides specific duty would afford to the american manufacturer the incidental advantage to which he be fairly entitle under a revenue tariff the present system be a slide scale to he disadvantage under it when price be high and business prosperous the duty rise in amount when he least require they aid on the contrary when price fall and he be struggle against adversity the duty be diminish in the same proportion greatly to he injury neither would there be danger that a higher rate of duty than that intend by congress could be levy in the form of specific duty it would be easy to ascertain the average value of any import article for a series of year and instead of subject it to a _ ad valorem _ duty at a certain rate _ per centum _ to substitute in its place a equivalent specific duty by such a arrangement the consumer would not be injure it be true he might have to pay a little more duty on a give article in one year but if so he would pay a little less in another and in a series of year these would counterbalance each other and amount to the same thing so far as he interest be concern this inconvenience would be trifling when contrast with the additional security thus afford against fraud upon the revenue in which every consumer be directly interested i have throw out these suggestion as the fruit of my own observation to which congress in they better judgment will give such weight as they may justly deserve the report of the they be suppose to be and mail stage with passenger now pass and repass regularly twice in each week by a common wagon road between san francisco and st loui and memphi in less than twenty-five day the service have be as regularly perform as it be in former year between new york and this city whilst disclaim all authority to appropriate money for the construction of this road except that derive from the war-making power of the constitution there be important collateral consideration urge we to undertake the work as speedily as possible the first and most momentous of these be that such a road would be a powerful bond of union between the state east and west of the rocky mountain this be so self-evident as to require no illustration but again in a commercial point of view i consider this the great question of the day with the eastern front of we republic stretch along the atlantic and its western front along the pacific if all the part should be unite by a safe easy and rapid intercommunication we must necessarily command a very large proportion of the trade both of europe and asia we recent treaty with china and japan will open these rich and populous empire to we commerce and the history of the world prove that the nation which have gain possession of the trade with eastern asia have always become wealthy and powerful the peculiar geographical position of californium and we pacific possession invite american capital and enterprise into this fruitful field to reap the rich harvest however it be a indispensable prerequisite that we shall first have a railroad to convey and circulate its product throughout every portion of the union besides such a railroad through we temperate latitude which would not be impede by the frost and snow of winter nor by the tropical heat of summer would attract to itself much of the travel and the trade of all nation pass between europe and asia on the 21st of August last lieutenant jn maffit of the united state act prohibit the slave trade under the second section of this act the president be authorize to make such regulation and arrangement as he may deem expedient for the safe-keeping support and removal beyond the limit of the united state of all such negro mulatto or person of color capture by vessel of the united state as may be deliver to the marshal of the district into which they be bring and to appoint a proper person or person reside upon the coast of africa as agent or agent for receive the negro mulatto or person of color deliver from on board vessel seize in the prosecution of the slave trade by commander of united state arm vessel a doubt immediately arise as to the true construction of this act it be quite clear from its term that the president be authorize to provide for the safe-keeping support and removal of these negro up till the time of they delivery to the agent on the coast of africa but no express provision be make for they protection and support after they have reach the place of they destination still a agent be to be appoint to receive they in africa and it could not have be suppose that congress intend he should desert they at the moment they be receive and turn they loose on that inhospitable coast to perish for want of food or to become again the victim of the slave trade have this be the intention of congress the employment of a agent to receive they who be require to reside on the coast be unnecessary and they might have be land by we vessel anywhere in africa and leave expose to the suffering and the fate which would certainly await they mr monroe in he special message of December 17 1819 at the first session after the act be pass announce to congress what in he opinion be its true construction he believe it to be he duty under it to follow these unfortunate into africa and make provision for they there until they should be able to provide for themselves in communicate this interpretation of the act to congress he state that some doubt have be entertain as to its true intent and meaning and he submit the question to they so that they might should it be deem advisable amend the same before further proceedings be have under it nothing be do by congress to explain the act and mr monroe proceed to carry it into execution accord to he own interpretation this then become the practical construction when the african from on board the _ echo _ be deliver to the marshal at charleston it become my duty to consider what disposition ought to be make of they under the law for many reason it be expedient to remove they from that locality as speedily as possible although the conduct of the authority and citizen of charleston in give countenance to the execution of the law be just what might have be expect from they high character yet a prolonged continuance of 300 african in the immediate vicinity of that city could not have fail to become a source of inconvenience and anxiety to its inhabitant where to send they be the question there be no portion of the coast of africa to which they could be remove with any regard to humanity except to liberium under these circumstance a agreement be enter into with the colonization society on the 7th of September last a copy of which be herewith transmit under which the society engage for the consideration of $ 45000 to receive these african in liberium from the agent of the united state and furnish they during the period of one year thereafter with comfortable shelter clothing provision and medical attendance cause the child to receive schooling and all whether child or adult to be instruct in the art of civilized life suitable to they condition this aggregate of $ 45000 be base upon a allowance of $ 150 for each individual and as there have be considerable mortality among they and may be more before they reach africa the society have agree in a equitable spirit to make such a deduction from the amount as under the circumstance may appear just and reasonable this can not be fix until we shall ascertain the actual number which may become a charge to the society it be also distinctly agree that under no circumstance shall this government be call upon for any additional expense the agent of the society manifest a laudable desire to conform to the wish of the government throughout the transaction they assure I that after a careful calculation they would be require to expend the sum of $ 150 on each individual in comply with the agreement and they would have nothing leave to remunerate they for they care trouble and responsibility at all event i could make no better arrangement and there be no other alternative during the period when the government itself through its own agent undertake the task of provide for capture negro in africa the cost per head be very much greater there have be no outstanding appropriation applicable to this purpose i could not advance any money on the agreement i therefore recommend that a appropriation may be make of the amount necessary to carry it into effect other capture of a similar character may and probably will be make by we naval force and i earnestly recommend that congress may amend the second section of the act of march 3 1819 so as to free its construction from the ambiguity which have so long exist and render the duty of the president plain in execute its provision i recommend to you favorable regard the local interest of the district of columbium as the residence of congress and the executive department of the government we can not fail to feel a deep concern in its welfare this be heighten by the high character and the peaceful and orderly conduct of its resident inhabitant i can not conclude without perform the agreeable duty of express my gratification that congress so kindly respond to the recommendation of my last annual message by afford I sufficient time before the close of they late session for the examination of all the bill present to I for approval this change in the practice of congress have prove to be a wholesome reform it exert a beneficial influence on the transaction of legislative business and elicit the general approbation of the country it enable congress to adjourn with that dignity and deliberation so become to the representative of this great republic without have crowd into general appropriation bill provision foreign to they nature and of doubtful constitutionality and expediency let I warmly and strongly commend this precedent establish by themselves as a guide to they proceedings during the present session jame buchanan special message washington _ December 7 1858 _ _ to the senate of the united state _ : i transmit to the senate for its consideration with a view to ratification a herewith submit the result of my investigation under the resolution of congress of march 10 and may 11 1858 in compliance with these resolution i have carefully examine the record of the court of inquiry in fifty-eight case and have arrive at the conclusion that twenty-three of the officer ought to remain in the position where they have be fix by the court of inquiry the record be very voluminous and the labor of examination in which i have be materially assist by the secretary of the navy the attorney-general and the commissioner of patent have consume much time under the act of January 17 1857 the court of inquiry be direct to investigate the physical mental professional and moral fitness of each officer who apply to they for relief these investigation it be my duty to review they have be very extensive and search as the senate will perceive from a examination of the record embrace in many instance almost the entire professional life of the individual from he first entrance into the service in the performance of my duty i find the greatest difficulty in decide what should be consider as moral fitness for the navy physical mental and professional fitness may be decide with a considerable degree of accuracy by a naval court of inquiry but the question of moral fitness be of a very different character there have be but one perfect standard of morality on earth and how far a departure from he precept and example must proceed in order to disqualify a officer for the naval service be a question on which a great difference of honest opinion must always exist on this question i have differ in several instance from the court of inquiry there be one nomination which i regret that i have not the power to present to the senate and this be in the case of commodore stewart he name stand on the register at the head of the list of captain in the navy until it be remove from this well-earned position by the retire board and place on the list of retired officer the deeply wounded feeling of this veteran officer who have contribute so much to the efficiency and glory of the navy from its infancy prevent he from apply for restoration to he rank and submit to a court of inquiry compose of he junior officer the question of he physical mental professional and moral fitness for the naval service i would ere this have recommend to congress the passage of a joint resolution to restore he to he former rank have i not believe this would more appropriately emanate from the legislative branch of government i transmit herewith to the senate the original record in the fifty-eight case to which i have refer after they shall have be examine by the senate i would respectfully request that they might be return to the navy department jame buchanan washington _
