session and the great urgency and importance of legislative action before its termination for the protection of american citizen and they property whilst in transit across the isthmus route between we atlantic and pacific possession render it my duty again to recall this subject to you notice i have heretofore present it in my annual message both in December 1857 and 1858 to which i beg leave to refer in the latter i state that -- the executive government of this country in its intercourse with foreign nation be limit to the employment of diplomacy alone when this fail it can proceed no further it can not legitimately resort to force without the direct authority of congress except in resist and repel hostile attack it would have no authority to enter the territory of nicaragua even to prevent the destruction of the transit and protect the life and property of we own citizen on they passage it be true that on a sudden emergency of this character the president would direct any armed force in the vicinity to march to they relief but in do this he would act upon he own responsibility under these circumstance i earnestly recommend to congress the passage of a act authorize the president under such restriction as they may deem proper to employ the land and naval force of the united state in prevent the transit from be obstruct or close by lawless violence and in protect the life and property of american citizen travel thereupon require at the same time that these force shall be withdraw the moment the danger shall have pass away without such a provision we citizen will be constantly expose to interruption in they progress and to lawless violence a similar necessity exist for the passage of such a act for the protection of the panama and tehuantepee route another subject equally important command the attention of the senate at the last session of congress the republic south of the united state on this continent have unfortunately be frequently in a state of revolution and civil war ever since they achieve they independence as one or the other party have prevail and obtain possession of the port open to foreign commerce they have seize and confiscate american vessel and they cargo in a arbitrary and lawless manner and exact money from american citizen by forced loan and other violent proceedings to enable they to carry on hostility the executive government of great britain france and other country possess the war-making power can promptly employ the necessary means to enforce immediate redress for similar outrage upon they subject not so the executive government of the united state if the president order a vessel of war to any of these port to demand prompt redress for outrage commit the offend party be well aware that in case of refusal the commander can do no more than remonstrate he can resort to no hostile act the question must then be refer to diplomacy and in many case adequate redress can never be obtain thus american citizen be deprive of the same protection under the flag of they country which the subject of other nation enjoy the remedy for this state of thing can only be supply by congress since the constitution have confide to that body alone the power to make war without the authority of congress the executive can not lawfully direct any force however near it may be to the scene of difficulty to enter the territory of mexico nicaragua or new granada for the purpose of defend the person and property of american citizen even though they may be violently assail whilst pass in peaceful transit over the tehuantepec nicaragua or panama route he can not without transcend he constitutional power direct a gun to be fire into a port or land a seaman or marine to protect the life of we countryman on shore or to obtain redress for a recent outrage on they property the bandit which infest we neighboring republic of mexico always claim to belong to one or other of the hostile party might make a sudden descent on vera cruz or on the tehuantepec route and he would have no power to employ the force on shipboard in the vicinity for they relief either to prevent the plunder of we merchant or the destruction of the transit in reference to country where the local authority be strong enough to enforce the law the difficulty here indicate can seldom happen but where this be not the case and the local authority do not possess the physical power even if they possess the will to protect we citizen within they limit recent experience have show that the american executive should itself be authorize to render this protection such a grant of authority thus limit in its extent could in no just sense be regard as a transfer of the war-making power to the executive but only as a appropriate exercise of that power by the body to whom it exclusively belong the riot at panama in 1856 in which a great number of we citizen lose they life furnish a pointed illustration of the necessity which may arise for the exertion of this authority i therefore earnestly recommend to congress on whom the responsibility exclusively rest to pass a law before they adjournment confer on the president the power to protect the life and property of american citizen in the case which i have indicate under such restriction and condition as they may deem advisable the knowledge that such a law exist would of itself go far to prevent the outrage which it be intend to redress and to render the employment of force unnecessary without this the president may be place in a painful position before the meeting of the next congress in the present disturbed condition of mexico and one or more of the other republic south of we no person can foresee what occurrence may take place before that period in case of emergency we citizen see that they do not enjoy the same protection with subject of european government will have just cause to complain on the other hand should the executive interpose and especially should the result prove disastrous and valuable life be lose he might subject himself to severe censure for have assume a power not confide to he by the constitution it be to guard against this contingency that i now appeal to congress have thus recommend to congress a measure which i deem necessary and expedient for the interest and honor of the country i leave the whole subject to they wisdom and discretion jame buchanan washington _ February 18 1859 _ _ to the senate of the united state _ : i transmit to the senate for its consideration with a view to ratification two convention the credit of the country this be the last day of the present congress and no provision have yet be make for the payment of appropriation and to meet the outstanding treasury note issue under the authority of law from the information which have already be communicate to congress by the secretary of the treasury it be manifest that the ordinary receipt into the treasury even under the most favorable circumstance will scarcely meet the ordinary expense of the government during the remainder of the present fiscal year end on the 30th of June at that time nearly eighteen million of treasury note will have become due and many of those not yet due be daily pay for duty at the different port and there will be no means in the treasury to meet they thus the country which be full of resource will be dishonor before the world and the american people who be a debt-paying people will be disgrace by the omission on we part to do we duty it be impossible to avoid this catastrophe unless we make provision this very day to meet the lawful demand on the public treasury if this be the first instead of the last session of a congress the case would be different you might then be convene by proclamation for to-morrow morning but there be now thirteen state of the union entitle to seventy-eight representative in which none have be elect it will therefore be impracticable for a large majority of these state to elect they member before the treasury shall be compel to stop payment under these circumstance i earnestly recommend to congress to make provision within the few remain hour of the session for the preservation of the public credit the urgency of the case not only justify but demand that if necessary this shall be do by a separate bill we ought to incur no risk when the good faith of the country be at stake jame buchanan veto message -lrb- 10 -rrb- -lrb- footnote 10 : the first be a pocket veto -rrb- washington _ January 7 1859 _ _ to the house of representative _ : on the last day of the last session of congress as appear by the journal of the house of representative a joint resolution in regard to the carry the united state mail from saint joseph missouri to placerville californium be present to I for my approval this resolution authorize and direct the postmaster-general to order a increase of speed upon say route require the mail to be carry through in thirty day instead of thirty-eight day accord to the exist contract : _ provide _ the same can be do upon a _ pro rata _ increase of compensation to the contractor i do not approve this joint resolution : first because it be present to I at so late a period that i have not the time necessary on the day of the adjournment of the last session for a investigation of the subject besides no injury could result to the public as the postmaster-general already possess the discretionary power under exist law to increase the speed upon this as well as all other mail route second because the postmaster-general at the moment in the capitol inform I that the contractor themselves have offer to increase the speed on this route to thirty instead of thirty-eight day at a less cost than that authorize by the joint resolution upon subsequent examination it have be ascertain at the post-office department that they bid which be still depend propose to perform this service for a sum less by $ 49000 than that authorize by the resolution jame buchanan washington city _ February 24 1859 _ _ to the house of representative of the united state _ : i return with my objection to the donation of 20000 acre for each additional representative to which any state may be entitle under the census of 1860 accord to a report from the interior department base upon the present number of senator and representative the land give to the state amount to 6060000 acre and they value at the minimum government price of $ 125 per acre to $ 7575000 the object of this gift as state by the bill be the endowment support and maintenance of at least one college -lrb- in each state -rrb- where the lead object shall be without exclude other scientific or classical study to teach such branch of will be close until after the funeral isaac toucey _ secretary of the navy _ third annual message washington city _ December 19 1859 _ _ fellow-citizen of the senate and house of representative _ : we deep and heartfelt gratitude be due to that almighty power which have bestow upon we such varied and numerous blessing throughout the past year the general health of the country have be excellent we harvest have be unusually plentiful and prosperity smile throughout the land indeed notwithstanding we demerit we have much reason to believe from the past event in we history that we have enjoy the special protection of divine providence ever since we origin as a nation we have be expose to many threatening and alarming difficulty in we progress but on each successive occasion the impending cloud have be dissipate at the moment it appear ready to burst upon we head and the danger to we institution have pass away may we ever be under the divine guidance and protection whilst it be the duty of the president from time to time to give to congress information of the state of the union i shall not refer in detail to the recent sad and bloody occurrence at harper ferry still it be proper to observe that these event however bad and cruel in themselves derive they chief importance from the apprehension that they be but symptom of a incurable disease in the public mind which may break out in still more dangerous outrage and terminate at last in a open war by the north to abolish slavery in the south whilst for myself i entertain no such apprehension they ought to afford a solemn warning to we all to beware of the approach of danger we union be a stake of such inestimable value as to demand we constant and watchful vigilance for its preservation in this view let I implore my countryman north and south to cultivate the ancient feeling of mutual forbearance and good will toward each other and strive to allay the demon spirit of sectional hatred and strife now alive in the land this advice proceed from the heart of a old public functionary whose service commence in the last generation among the wise and conservative statesman of that day now nearly all pass away and whose first and dearest earthly wish be to leave he country tranquil prosperous unite and powerful we ought to reflect that in this age and especially in this country there be a incessant flux and reflux of public opinion question which in they day assume a most threatening aspect have now nearly go from the memory of man they be volcano burn out and on the lava and ash and squalid scorium of old eruption grow the peaceful olive the cheer vine and the sustain corn such in my opinion will prove to be the fate of the present sectional excitement should those who wisely seek to apply the remedy continue always to confine they effort within the pale of the constitution if this course be pursue the exist agitation on the subject of domestic slavery like everything human will have its day and give place to other and less threatening controversy public opinion in this country be all-powerful and when it reach a dangerous excess upon any question the good sense of the people will furnish the corrective and bring it back within safe limit still to hasten this auspicious result at the present crisis we ought to remember that every rational creature must be presume to intend the natural consequence of he own teaching those who announce abstract doctrine subversive of the constitution and the union must not be surprise should they heated partisan advance one step further and attempt by violence to carry these doctrine into practical effect in this view of the subject it ought never to be forget that however great may have be the political advantage result from the union to every portion of we common country these would all prove to be as nothing should the time ever arrive when they can not be enjoy without serious danger to the personal safety of the people of fifteen member of the confederacy if the peace of the domestic fireside throughout these state should ever be invade if the mother of family within this extensive region should not be able to retire to rest at night without suffer dreadful apprehension of what may be they own fate and that of they child before the morning it would be vain to recount to such a people the political benefit which result to they from the union self-preservation be the first instinct of nature and therefore any state of society in which the sword be all the time suspend over the head of the people must at last become intolerable but i indulge in no such gloomy foreboding on the contrary i firmly believe that the event at harper ferry by cause the people to pause and reflect upon the possible peril to they cherish institution will be the means under providence of allay the exist excitement and prevent further outbreak of a similar character they will resolve that the constitution and the union shall not be endanger by rash counsel know that should the silver cord be loose or the golden bowl be break at the fountain human power could never reunite the scatter and hostile fragment i cordially congratulate you upon the final settlement by the supreme court of the united state of the question of slavery in the territory which have present a aspect so truly formidable at the commencement of my administration the right have be establish of every citizen to take he property of any kind include slave into the common territory belong equally to all the state of the confederacy and to have it protect there under the federal constitution neither congress nor a territorial legislature nor any human power have any authority to annul or impair this vested right the supreme judicial tribunal of the country which be a coordinate branch of the government have sanction and affirm these principle of constitutional law so manifestly just in themselves and so well calculate to promote peace and harmony among the state it be a striking proof of the sense of justice which be inherent in we people that the property in slave have never be disturb to my knowledge in any of the territory even throughout the late trouble in kansas there have not be any attempt as i be credibly inform to interfere in a single instance with the right of the master have any such attempt be make the judiciary would doubtless have afford a adequate remedy should they fail to do this hereafter it will then be time enough to strengthen they hand by further legislation have it be decide that either congress or the territorial legislature possess the power to annul or impair the right to property in slave the evil would be intolerable in the latter event there would be a struggle for a majority of the member of the legislature at each successive election and the sacred rights of property hold under the federal constitution would depend for the time be on the result the agitation would thus be render incessant whilst the territorial condition remain and its baneful influence would keep alive a dangerous excitement among the people of the several state thus have the status of a territory during the intermediate period from its first settlement until it shall become a state be irrevocably fix by the final decision of the supreme court fortunate have this be for the prosperity of the territory as well as the tranquillity of the state now emigrant from the north and the south the east and the west will meet in the territory on a common platform have bring with they that species of property best adapt in they own opinion to promote they welfare from natural cause the slavery question will in each case soon virtually settle itself and before the territory be prepare for admission as a state into the union this decision one way or the other will have be a foregone conclusion meanwhile the settlement of the new territory will proceed without serious interruption and its progress and prosperity will not be endanger or retard by violent political struggle when in the progress of event the inhabitant of any territory shall have reach the number require to form a state they will then proceed in a regular manner and in the exercise of the rights of popular sovereignty to form a constitution preparatory to admission into the union after this have be do to employ the language of the kansa and nebraska act they shall be receive into the union with or without slavery as they constitution may prescribe at the time of they admission this sound principle have happily be recognize in some form or other by a almost unanimous vote of both house of the last congress all lawful means at my command have be employ and shall continue to be employ to execute the law against the african slave trade after a most careful and rigorous examination of we coast and a thorough investigation of the subject we have not be able to discover that any slave have be import into the united state except the cargo by the _ wanderer _ numbering between three and four hundred those engage in this unlawful enterprise have be rigorously prosecute but not with as much success as they crime have deserve a number of they be still under prosecution we history prove that the father of the republic in advance of all other nation condemn the african slave trade it be notwithstanding deem expedient by the framer of the constitution to deprive congress of the power to prohibit the migration or importation of such person as any of the state now exist shall think proper to admit prior to the year 1808 it will be see that this restriction on the power of congress be confine to such state only as might think proper to admit the importation of slave it do not extend to other state or to the trade carry on abroad accordingly we find that so early as the 22d march 1794 congress pass a act impose severe penalty and punishment upon citizen and resident of the united state who should engage in this they benefit and to prohibit by they own law this trade at any time they think proper previous to 1808 several of they exercise this right before that period and among they some contain the greatest number of slave this give to congress the immediate power to act in regard to all such state because they themselves have remove the constitutional barrier congress accordingly pass a act on 28th February 1803 to prevent the importation of certain person into certain state where by the law thereof they admission be prohibit in this manner the importation of african slave into the united state on the 2d of march 1807 they pass a act to take effect from and after the 1st day of January 1808 prohibit the importation of african slave into the united state this be follow by subsequent act of a similar character to which i need not specially refer such be the principle and such the practice of we ancestor more than fifty year ago in regard to the african slave trade it do not occur to the if this be not the case the framer of the constitution have expend much labor in vain have they imagine that congress would possess no power to prohibit the trade either before or after 1808 they no state can employ in time of peace without the consent of congress these act of congress it be believe have with very rare and insignificant exception accomplish they purpose for a period of more african race the light and the blessing of christianity have be extend to they and both they moral and physical condition have be greatly improve reopen the trade and it would be difficult to determine whether the effect would be more deleterious on the interest of the master or on those of the native-born slave of the evil to the master the one most to be dread would be the introduction of wild heathen and ignorant barbarian among the sober orderly and quiet slave whose ancestor have be on the soil for several generation this might tend to barbarize demoralize and exasperate the whole mass and produce most deplorable consequence the effect upon the exist slave would if possible be still more deplorable at present he be treat with kindness and humanity he be well feed well clothed and not overworked he condition be incomparably better than that of the coolie which modern nation of high civilization have employ as a substitute for african slave both the philanthropy and itself if we should reopen the slave trade this would give the trade a impulse and extension which it have never have even in its palmiest day the numerous victim require to supply it would convert confer it would violate the constitution that it would be a transfer of the war-making or strictly speak the war-declaring power to the executive if this be well found it would of course be conclusive a very brief examination however will place this objection at rest congress possess the sole and exclusive power under the constitution to declare war they alone can raise and support army and provide and maintain a navy but after congress shall have declare war and provide the force necessary to carry it on the president as commander in chief of the army and navy can alone employ this force in make war against the enemy this be the plain language and history prove that it be the well-known intention of the framer of the constitution it will not be deny that the general power to declare war be without limitation and embrace within itself not only what writer on the law of nation term a public or perfect war but also a imperfect war and in short every species of hostility however confine or limit without the authority of congress the president can not fire a hostile gun in any case except to repel the attack of a enemy it will not be doubt that under this power congress could if they think proper authorize the president to employ the force at he command to seize a vessel belong to a american citizen which have be illegally and unjustly capture in a foreign port and restore it to its owner but can congress only act after the fact after the mischief have be do have they no power to confer upon the president the authority in advance to furnish instant redress should such a case afterwards occur must they wait until the mischief have be do and can they apply the remedy only when it be too late to confer this authority to meet future case under circumstance strictly specify be as clearly within the war-declaring power as such a authority confer upon the president by act of congress after the deed have be do in the progress of a great nation many exigency must arise imperatively require that congress should authorize the president to act promptly on certain condition which may or may not afterwards arise we history have already present a number of such case i shall refer only to the latest under the resolution of June 2 1858 for the adjustment of difficulty with the republic of paraguay the president be authorize to adopt such measure and use such force as embrace within the power to declare war now if this conditional and contingent power could be constitutionally confer upon the president in the case of paraguay why may it not be confer for the sixty day more be allow for the settlement of they account before the department could be call upon for payment the great difficulty and the great hardship consist in the failure to provide for the payment of the deficiency in the fiscal year end the 30th June 1859 the department have enter into contract in obedience to exist law for the service of that fiscal year and the contractor be fairly entitle to they compensation as it become due the deficiency as state in the bill amount to $ 3838728 but after a careful settlement of all these account it have be ascertain that it amount to $ December last in the meantime the contractor themselves under these try circumstance have behave in a manner worthy of all commendation they have one resource in the midst of they embarrassment after the amount due to each of they have be ascertain and finally settle accord to law this become a specific debt of record against the united state which enable they to borrow money on this unquestionable security still they be oblige to pay interest in consequence of the default of congress and on every principle of justice ought to receive interest from the government this interest should commence from the date when a warrant would have issue for the payment of the principal have a appropriation be make for this purpose calculate up to the 1st December it will not exceed $ 96660 -- a sum not to be take into account when contrast with the great difficulty and embarrassment of a public and private character both to the people and the state which would have result from convene and hold a special session of congress for these reason i recommend the passage of a bill at as early a day as may be practicable to provide for the payment of the amount with interest due to these last-mentioned contractor as well as to make the necessary appropriation for the service of the post-office department for the current fiscal year the failure to pass the post-office bill necessarily give birth to serious reflection congress by refuse to pass the general appropriation bill necessary to carry on the government may not only arrest its action but might even destroy its existence the army the navy the judiciary in short every department of the government can no longer perform they function if congress refuse the money necessary for they support if this failure should teach the country the necessity of elect a full congress in sufficient time to enable the president to convene they in any emergency even immediately after the old congress have expire it will have be productive of great good in a time of sudden and alarming danger foreign or domestic which all nation must expect to encounter in they progress the very salvation of we institution may be stake upon the assemble of congress without delay if under such circumstance the president should find himself in the condition in which he be place at the close of the last congress with nearly half the state of the union destitute of representative the consequence might be disastrous i therefore recommend to congress to carry into effect the provision of the constitution on this subject and to pass a law appoint some day previous to the 4th march in each year of odd number for the election of representative throughout all the state they have already appoint a day for the election of elector for president and vice-president and this measure have be approve by the country i would again express a most decide opinion in favor of the construction of a pacific railroad for the reason state in my two last annual message when i reflect upon what would be the defenseless condition of we state and territory west of the rocky mountain in case of a war with a naval power sufficiently strong to interrupt all intercourse with they by the route across the isthmus i be still more convinced than ever of the vast importance of this railroad i have never doubt the constitutional competency of congress to provide for its construction but this exclusively under the war-making power besides the constitution expressly require as a imperative duty that the united state shall protect each of they -lrb- the state -rrb- against invasion i be at a loss to conceive how this protection can be afford to californium and oregon against such a naval power by any other means i repeat the opinion contain in my last annual message that it would be inexpedient for the government to undertake this great work by agent of its own appointment and under its direct and exclusive control this would increase the patronage of the executive to a dangerous extent and would foster a system of jobbing and corruption which no vigilance on the part of federal official could prevent the construction of this road ought therefore to be intrust to incorporated company or other agency who would exercise that active and vigilant supervision over it which can be inspire alone by a sense of corporate and individual interest i venture to assert that the additional cost of transporting troops munitions of war and necessary supplies for the army across the vast intervene plain to we possession on the pacific coast would be greater in such a war than the whole amount require to construct the road and yet this resort would after all be inadequate for they defense and protection we have yet scarcely recover from the habit of extravagant expenditure produce by we overflow treasury during several year prior to the commencement of my administration the financial reverse which we have since experienced ought to teach we all to scrutinize we expenditure with the greatest vigilance and to reduce they to the lowest possible point the executive department of the government have devote themselves to the accomplishment of this object with considerable success as will appear from they different report and estimate to these i invite the scrutiny of congress for the purpose of reduce they still lower if this be practicable consistent with the great public interest of the country in aid of the policy of retrenchment i pledge myself to examine closely the bill appropriate land or money so that if any of these should inadvertently pass both house as must sometimes be the case i may afford they a opportunity for reconsideration at the same time we ought never to forget that true public economy consist not in withhold the means necessary to accomplish important national object confide to we by the constitution but in take care that the money appropriate for these purpose shall be faithfully and frugally expend it will appear from the report of the secretary of the treasury that it be extremely doubtful to say the least whether we shall be able to pass through the present and the next fiscal year without provide additional revenue this can only be accomplish by strictly confine the appropriation within the estimate of the different department without make a allowance for any additional expenditure which congress may think proper in they discretion to authorize and without provide for the redemption of any portion of the $ 20000000 of treasury note which have be already issue in the event of a deficiency which i consider probable this ought never to be supply by a resort to additional loan it would be a ruinous practice in the day of peace and prosperity to go on increase the national debt to meet the ordinary expense of the government this policy would cripple we resource and impair we credit in case the existence of war should render it necessary to borrow money should such a deficiency occur as i apprehend i would recommend that the necessary revenue be raise by a increase of we present duty on import i need not repeat the opinion express in my last annual message as to the best mode and manner of accomplish this object and shall now merely observe that these have since undergo no change the report of the secretary of the treasury will consideration of the senate with a view to ratification a treaty of friendship commerce and navigation between the united state and the republic of hondura sign by the plenipotentiary of the party in this city on the 28th day of last month the fourteenth article of this treaty be a exact copy of the supplemental article of the treaty of friendship commerce and navigation between great britain and the republic of hondura date 26th day of August 1856 with the necessary change in name and date under this article the government and people of the united state will enjoy in the fullest and most satisfactory manner the use of the hondura interoceanic railway in consideration of which the united state recognize the rights of sovereignty and property of hondura over the line of the road and guarantee its neutrality and when the road shall have be complete equally engage in conjunction with hondura to protect the same from interruption seizure or unjust confiscation from whatever quarter the attempt may proceed this treaty be in accordance with the policy inaugurate by the government of the united state and in a especial manner by the senate in the year 1846 and several treaty have be conclude to carry it into effect it be simple and may be embrace in a few word on the one side a grant of free and uninterrupted transit for the government and people of the united state over the transit route across the isthmus and on the other a guaranty of the neutrality and protection of these route not only for the benefit of the republic through which they pass but in the language of we treaty with new granada in order to secure to themselves the tranquil and constant enjoyment of these inter-oceanic communication the first in the series of these treaty be that with new granada of the 12th December 1846 this treaty be conclude before we acquisition of californium and when we interest on the pacific coast be of far less magnitude than at the present day for year before this period however the route across the isthmus have attract the serious attention of this government this treaty after grant we the right of transit across the isthmus of panama in the most ample term bind this government to guarantee to new granada the perfect neutrality of the before-mentioned isthmus with the view that the free transit from the one to the other sea may not be interrupted or embarrassed in any future time while this treaty exist in one respect it go further than any of its successor because it not only guarantee the neutrality of the route itself but the rights of sovereignty and property of new granada over the entire province of panama it be worthy of remark that when it be send to the senate it be accompany by a message of president polk date February 10 1847 in which the attention of that body be especially call to these important stipulation of the thirty-fifth article and in which it be state moreover that we charg d'affaire who negotiate the treaty act in this particular upon he own responsibility and without instruction under these circumstance the treaty be approve by the senate and the transit policy to which i have refer be deliberately adopt a copy of the executive document -lrb- confidential -rrb- twenty-ninth congress second session contain this message of president polk and the papers which accompany it be hereto annex the next in order of time of these treaty of transit and guaranty be that of the 19th April 1850 with great britain commonly call the clayton and bulwer treaty this treaty in affirmance of the policy of the new granada treaty establish a general principle which have ever since i believe guide the proceedings of both government the eighth article of that treaty contain the follow stipulation : the government of the united state have not only desire in enter into this convention to accomplish a particular object but also to establish a general principle they hereby agree to extend they protection by treaty stipulation to any other practicable communication whether by canal or railway across the isthmus which connect north and south america and especially to the interoceanic communication should the same prove to be practicable whether by canal or railway which be now propose to be establish by the way of tehuantepec or panama and that the say -- canal or railway shall also be open on like term to the citizen and subject of every other state which be willing to grant thereto such protection as the united state and great britain propose to afford the united state in a short time after the clayton and bulwer treaty be conclude carry this stipulation in regard to the tehuantepec route into effect by they treaty with mexico of the 30th December 1853 the eighth article of this treaty after grant to we the transit privilege therein mention stipulate that the mexican government have agree to protect with its whole power the prosecution preservation and security of the work the united state may extend its protection as it shall judge wise to use it when it may feel sanction and warrant by the public or international law this be a sweeping grant of power to the united state which no nation ought to have concede but which it be believe have be confine within safe limit by we treaty with mexico now before the senate such be believe to be the established policy of the government at the commencement of this administration viz the grant of transit in we favor and the guaranty of we protection as a equivalent this guaranty can never be dangerous under we form of government because it can never be carry into execution without the express authority of congress still stand on the face of treaty as it do it deter all evil-disposed party from interfere with these route under such circumstance the attention of the executive be early turn to the nicaragua route as in many respects the most important and valuable to the citizen of we country in conclude a treaty to secure we rights of transit over this route i experience many difficulty which i need not now enumerate because they be detail in different message to congress finally a treaty be negotiate exactly in accordance with the established policy of the government and the view of the executive and clear from the embarrassment which might arise under the phraseology of previous treaty the fourteenth article of the treaty contain a full clear and specific grant of the right of transit to the united state and they citizen and be believe to be perfectly unexceptionable the fifteenth article instead of leave one equivalent duty of protection general and unlimited as in we treaty with new granada and in the clayton and bulwer treaty or instead of that general right assure to the government in the mexican treaty of extend its protection as it shall itself judge wise when it may feel sanction and warrant by the public or international law confines the interference concede within just and specific limit under the sixteenth article of this treaty the government of the united state have no right to interpose for the protection of the nicaragua route except with the consent or at the request of the government of nicaragua or of the minister thereof at washington or of the competent legally appoint local authority civil or military and when in the opinion of the government of nicaragua the necessity cease such force shall be immediately withdraw nothing can be more carefully guard than this provision no force can be employ unless upon the request of the government of nicaragua and it must be immediately withdraw whenever in the opinion of that government the necessity cease when congress shall come to adopt the measure necessary to carry this provision of the treaty into effect they can guard it from any abuse which may possibly arise the general policy contain in these article although inaugurate by the united state have be fully adopt by the government of great britain and france the plenipotentiary of both these government have recently negotiate treaty with nicaragua which be but transcript of the treaty between the united state and nicaragua now before the senate the treaty with france have be ratify it be understand by both the french and nicaraguan government and be now in operation that with great britain have be delay by other negotiation in nicaragua but it be believe that these be now conclude and that the ratification of the british treaty will soon therefore be exchange it be presume that no objection will be make to the exceptional case of the sixteenth article which be only intend to provide for the landing of sailor or marine from we vessel which may happen to be within reach of the point of difficulty in order to protect the life and property of citizen of the united state from unforeseen and imminent danger the same consideration may be suggest with respect to the fifth article of the treaty with mexico which be also pend before the senate this article be a exact copy of the sixteenth article just refer to of the treaty with nicaragua the treaty with hondura which be now submit to the senate follow on this subject the language of the british treaty with that republic and be not therefore identical in its term with the nicaraguan and mexican treaty the same policy however have be adopt in all of they and it will not fail i be persuade to receive from the senate all that consideration which it so eminently deserve the importance to the united state of secure free and safe transit route across the american isthmus can not well be overestimate these route be of great interest of course to all commercial nation but they be especially so to we from we geographical and political position as a american state and because they furnish a necessary communication between we atlantic and pacific state and territory the government of the united state can never permit these route to be permanently interrupted nor can it safely allow they to pass under the control of other rival nation while it seek no exclusive privilege upon they for itself it can never consent to be make tributary to they use to any european power it be worthy of consideration however whether to some extent it would not necessarily become so if after great britain and france have adopt we policy and make treaty with the isthmian government in pursuance of it we should ourselves reconsider it and refuse to pursue it in the treaty of the united state i might add that the opening of these transit route can not fail to extend the trade and commerce of the united state with the country through which they pass to afford a outlet and a market for we manufacture within they territory to encourage american citizen to develop they vast store of mining and mineral wealth for we benefit and to introduce among they a wholesome american influence calculate to prevent revolution and to render they government stable jame buchanan washington _ April 10 1860 _ _ to the house of representative _ : i communicate herewith a report from the secretary of state in reply to the resolution of the house of 1858 i express my opinion in regard to the construction of the act of the 3d march 1819 in addition to the act prohibit the slave trade so far as the same be applicable to the present case from this i make the follow extract : under the second section of this act the president be authorize to make such regulation and arrangement as he may deem expedient for the safe-keeping support and removal appoint a proper person or person reside upon the coast of africa as agent or agent for receive the negro mulatto or person of color deliver from on board vessel seize in the prosecution of the slave trade by commander of united state arm vessel a doubt immediately arise as to the true construction of this act it be quite clear from its term that the president be authorize to provide for the safe-keeping support and removal of these negro up till the time of they delivery to the agent on the coast of africa but no express provision be make for they protection and support after they have reach the place of they destination still a agent be to be appoint to receive they in africa and it could not have be suppose that congress intend he should desert they at the moment they be receive and turn they loose on that inhospitable coast to perish for want of food or to become again the victim of the slave trade have this be the intention of congress the employment of a agent to receive they who be require to reside on the coast be unnecessary and they might have be land by we vessel anywhere in africa and leave expose to the suffering and the fate which would certainly await they mr monroe in he special message of December 17 1819 at the first session after the act be pass announce to congress what in he opinion be its true construction he believe it to be he duty under it to follow these unfortunate into africa and make provision for they there until they should be able to provide for themselves in communicate this interpretation of the act to congress he state that some doubt have be entertain as to its true intent and meaning and he submit the question to they so that they might should it be deem advisable amend the same before further proceedings be have under it nothing be do by congress to explain the act and mr monroe proceed to carry it into execution accord to he own interpretation this then become the practical construction adopt this construction of president monroe i enter into a agreement with the colonization society date 7th September 1858 to receive the african which have be capture on the slaver _ echo _ from the agent of the united state in liberium to furnish they during the period of one year thereafter with comfortable shelter clothing and provision and to cause they to be instruct in the art of civilized life suitable to they condition at the rate of $ 150 for each individual it be believe that within that period they would be prepare to become citizen of liberium and to take care of themselves as congress be not then in session and as there be no outstanding appropriation applicable to this purpose the society be oblige to depend for payment on the future action of that body i recommend this appropriation and $ 75000 be grant by the act of 3d march 1859 -lrb- the consular and diplomatic bill -rrb- to enable the president of the united state to carry into effect the act of congress of 3d march 1819 and any subsequent act now in force for the suppression of the slave trade of this appropriation there remain unexpended the sum of $ 2435090 after deduct from it a advance make by the secretary of the interior out of the judiciary fund of $ 1134810 i regret to say that under the mode adopt in regard to the african capture on board the _ echo _ the expense will be large but this seem to a great extent to be inevitable without a violation of the law of humanity the expenditure upon this scale for those capture on board the _ wildfire _ will not be less than $ 100000 and may considerably exceed that sum still it ought to be observe that during the period when the government itself through its own agent undertake the task of provide for capture negro in africa the cost per head be much greater than that which i agree to pay the colonization society but it will not be sufficient for congress to limit the amount appropriate to the case of the _ wildfire _ it be probable judge from the increase activity of the slave trade and the vigilance of we cruiser that several similar capture may be make before the end of the year a appropriation ought therefore to be grant large enough to cover such contingency the period have arrive when it be indispensable to provide some specific legislation for the guidance of the executive on this subject with this view i would suggest that congress might authorize the president to enter into a general agreement with the colonization society bind they to receive on the coast of africa from a agent there all the capture african which may be deliver to he and to maintain they for a limited period upon such term and condition as may combine humanity toward these unfortunate with a just economy this would obviate the necessity of make a new bargain with every new capture and would prevent delay and avoid expense in the disposition of the capture the law might then provide that in all case where this may be practicable the captor should carry the negro directly to africa and deliver they to the american agent there afterwards bring the capture vessel to the united state for adjudication the capture officer in case he should bring he prize directly to the united state ought to be require to land the negro in some one or more port to be designate by congress where the prevail health throughout the year be good at these port cheap but permanent accommodation might be provide for the negro until they could be send away without incur the expense of erect such accommodation at every port where the capture officer may think proper to enter on the present occasion these negro have be bring to key west and accord to the estimate present by the marshal of the southern district of florida to the secretary of the interior the cost of provide temporary quarter for they will be $ 2500 and the aggregate expense for the single month of may will amount to $ 12000 but this be far from be the worst evil within a few week the yellow fever will most probably prevail at key west and hence the marshal urge they removal from they present quarter at a early day which must be do in any event as soon as practicable for these reason i earnestly commend this subject to the immediate attention of congress i transmit herewith a copy of the letter and estimate of fernando j moreno marshal of the southern district of florida to the secretary of the interior dated 10th may 1860 together with a copy of the letter of the secretary of the interior to myself date 16th may it be truly lamentable that great britain and the united state should be oblige to expend such a vast amount of blood and treasure for the suppression of the african slave trade and this when the only portion of the civilized world where it be tolerate and encourage be the spanish island of cuba and porto rico jame buchanan washington _ may 22 1860 _ _ to the senate and house of representative _ : i transmit herewith the copy of a letter a act make appropriation for sundry civil expense of the government for the year end the 30th of June 1861 in notify the house of my approval of this bill i deem it proper under the peculiar for the completion of the washington aqueduct $ 500000 to be expend accord to the plan and estimate of captain meig and under he superintendence : _ provide _ that the office of engineer of the potomac waterworks be hereby abolish and its duty shall hereafter be discharge by the chief engineer of the washington aqueduct to this appropriation for a wise and beneficial object i have not the sufficient for the purpose it be now discover however that it will require half a million more _ for the completion of the washington aqueduct _ and this ought to be grant the captain meig to whom the bill refer be montgomery c meig a captain in the corps of engineer of the army of the united state who have superintend this work from its commencement under the authority of the late and present secretary of war have this appropriation be make in the usual form no difficulty could have arise upon it this bill however annex a declaration to the appropriation that the money be to be expend under the superintendence of captain meig the first aspect in which this clause present itself to my mind be that it interfere with the right of the president to be commander in chief of the army and navy of the united state if this have really be the case there would have be a end to the question upon further examination i deem it impossible that congress could have intend to interfere with the clear right of the president to command the army and to order its officer to any duty he might deem most expedient for the public interest if they could withdraw a officer from the command of the president and select he for the performance of a executive duty they might upon the same principle annex to a appropriation to carry on a war a condition require it not to be use for the defense of the country unless a particular person of its own selection should command the army it be impossible that congress could have have such a intention and therefore accord to my construction of the clause in question it merely designate captain meig as its preference for the work without intend to deprive the president of the power to order he to any other army duty for the performance of which he might consider he better adapt still whilst this clause may not be and i believe be not a violation of the constitution yet how destructive it would be to all proper subordination and how demoralize its effect upon the morale of the army if it should become a precedent for future legislation officer might then be find instead of perform they appropriate duty besiege the hall of congress for the purpose of obtain special favor and choice place by legislative enactment under these circumstance i have deem it but fair to inform congress that whilst i do not consider the bill unconstitutional this be only because in my opinion congress do not intend by the language which they have employ to interfere with my absolute authority to order captain meig to any other service i might deem expedient my perfect right still remain notwithstanding the clause to send he away from washington to any part of the union to superintend the erection of a fortification or on any other appropriate duty it have be allege i think without sufficient cause that this clause be unconstitutional because it have create a new office and have appoint captain meig to perform its duty if it have do this it would have be a clear question because congress have no right to appoint to any office this be specially confer upon the president and senate it be evident that congress intend nothing more by this clause than to express a decide opinion that captain meig should be continue in the employment to which he have be previously assign by competent authority it be not improbable that another question of grave importance may arise out of this clause be the appropriation conditional and will it fall provide i do not deem it proper that it shall be expend under the superintendence of captain meig this be a question which shall receive serious consideration because upon its decision may depend whether the completion of the waterworks shall be arrest for another season it be not probable that congress could have intend that this great and important work should depend upon the various casualty and vicissitude incident to the natural or official life of a single officer of the army this would be to make the work subordinate to the man and not the man to the work and to reverse we great axiomatic rule of principle not man i desire to express no opinion upon the subject should the question ever arise it shall have my serious consideration jame buchanan veto message -lrb- 13 -rrb- -lrb- footnote 13 : the message of February 1 and February 6 1860 be pocket veto -rrb- washington city _ February 1 1860 _ _ to the senate of the united state _ : on the last day of the last congress a bill which have pass both house entitle a act make a appropriation for deepen the channel over the st clair flat in the state of michigan be present to I for approval it be scarcely necessary to observe that during the closing hour of a session it be impossible for the president on the instant to examine into the merit or demerit of a important bill involve as this do grave question both of expediency and of constitutional power with that care and deliberation demand by he public duty as well as by the best interest of the country for this reason the constitution have in all case allow he ten day for deliberation because if a bill be present to he within the last ten day of the session he be not require to return it either with a approval or a veto but may retain it in which case it shall not be a law whilst a occasion can rarely occur when so long a period as ten day would be require to enable the president to decide whether he should approve or veto a bill yet to deny he even two day on important question before the adjournment of each session for this purpose as recommend by a former annual message would not only be unjust to he but a violation of the spirit of the constitution to require he to approve a bill when it be impossible he could examine into its merit would be to deprive he of the exercise of he constitutional discretion and convert he into a mere register of the decree of congress i therefore deem it a sufficient reason for have retain the bill in question that it be not present to I until the last day of the session since the termination of the last congress i have make a thorough examination of the question involve in the bill to deepen the channel over the st clair flat and now proceed to express the opinion which i have form upon the subject and 1 even if this have be a mere question of expediency it be to say the least extremely doubtful whether the bill ought to have be approve because the object which congress intend to accomplish by the appropriation which it contain of $ 55000 have be already substantially accomplished i do not mean to allege that the work have be complete in the best manner but it be sufficient for all practical purpose the st clair flat be form by the st clair river which empty into the lake of that name by several mouth and which form a bar or shoal on which in its natural state there be not more than 6 or 7 foot of water this shoal be interpose between the mouth of the river and the deep water of the lake a distance of 6000 foot and in its natural condition be a serious obstruction to navigation the obvious remedy for this be to deepen a channel through these flat by dredge so as to enable vessel which could navigate the lake and the river to pass through this intermediate channel this object have be already accomplish by previous appropriation but without my knowledge when the bill be present to I captain whipple of the topographical engineer to whom the expenditure of the last appropriation of $ 45000 for this purpose in 1856 be intrust in he annual report of the 1st October 1858 state that the dredging be discontinue on the 26th August 1858 when a channel have be cut average 275 foot wide with a depth vary from 12 to 15-1\/2 foot he say : so long as the lake retain its present height we may assume that the depth in the channel will be at least 13-1\/2 foot with this result highly creditable to captain whipple he observe that if he have be correctly inform all the lake navigator be gratified besides afterwards and during the autumn of 1858 the canadian government expend $ 20000 in deepen and widen the inner end of the channel excavate by the united state no complaint have be make previous to the passage of the bill of obstruction to the commerce and navigation across the st clair flat what then be the object of the appropriation propose by the bill it appear that the surface of the water in lake st clair have be gradually rise until in 1858 it have attain a elevation of 4 foot above what have be its level in 1841 it be infer whether correctly or not it be not for I to say that the surface of the water may gradually sink to the level of 1841 and in that event the water which be when the bill pass 13-1\/2 foot deep in the channel might sink to 9-1\/2 foot and thus obstruct the passage to provide for this contingency captain whipple suggest the propriety of place the subject before congress with a estimate for excavate a cut through the center of the new channel 150 foot in width and 4-1\/2 foot deep so as to obtain from the river to the lake a depth of 18 foot during season of extreme high water and 12 foot at period of extreme low water it be not allege that any present necessity exist for this narrower cut in the bottom of the present channel but it be infer that for the reason state it may hereafter become necessary captain whipple 's estimate amount to $ 50000 but congress by the bill have grant $ 55000 now if no other objection exist against this measure it would not seem necessary that the appropriation should have be make for the purpose indicate the channel be sufficiently deep for all practical purpose but from natural cause constantly operate in the lake which i need not explain this channel be peculiarly liable to fill up what be really require be that it should at interval be dredge out so as to preserve its present depth and surely the comparatively trifling expense necessary for this purpose ought not to be bear by the united state after a improvement have be once construct by appropriation from the treasury it be not too much to expect that it should be keep in repair by that portion of the commercial and navigate interest which enjoy its peculiar benefit the last report make by captain whipple date on the 13th September last have be submit to congress by the secretary of war and to this i would refer for information which be upon the whole favorable in relation to the present condition of the channel through the st clair flat 2 but the far more important question be do congress possess the power under the constitution to deepen the channel of river and to create and improve harbor for purpose of commerce the question of the constitutional argument which have be so often advance for my own opinion on this subject i might refer to president polk 's carefully consider message of the 15th December 1847 address to the house of representative whilst i be a member of he cabinet the power to pass the bill in question if it exist at all must be derive from the power to regulate commerce with foreign nation and among the several state and with the indian tribe the power to regulate : do this ever embrace the power to create or to construct to say that it do be to confound the meaning of word of well-known signification the word regulate have several shades of mean accord to its application to different subject but never do it approach the signification of creative power the regulate power necessarily presuppose the existence of something to be regulate as apply to commerce it signify accord to the lexicographer to subject to rule or restriction as to regulate trade etc the constitution itself be its own best expounder of the meaning of word employ by its framer thus congress have the power to coin money this be the creative power then immediately follow the power to regulate the value thereof -- that be of the coin money thus bring into existence the word regulate regulation and regulation occur several time in the constitution but always with this subordinate meaning thus after the creative power to raise and support army and to provide and maintain a navy have be confer upon congress then follow the power to make rule for the government and regulation of the land and naval force thus call into be so the constitution act upon the self-evident fact that commerce with foreign nation and among the several state and with the indian tribe already exist confer upon congress the power to regulate this commerce thus accord to chief justice marshall the power to regulate commerce be the power to prescribe the rule by which commerce be to be govern and mr madison in he veto message of the 3d march 1817 declare that -- the power to regulate commerce among the several state can not include a power to construct road and canal and to improve the navigation of water course in order to facilitate promote and secure such commerce without a latitude of construction depart from the ordinary import of the term strengthen by the known inconvenience which doubtless lead to the grant of this remedial power to congress we know from the history of the constitution what these inconvenience be different state admit foreign import at different rate of duty those which have prescribe a higher rate of duty for the purpose of increase they revenue be defeat in this object by the legislation of neighbor state admit the same foreign article at lower rate hence jealousy and dangerous rivalry have spring up between the different state it be chiefly in the desire to provide a remedy for these evil that the federal convention originate the constitution for this purpose confer upon congress the power to regulate commerce in such a manner that duty should be uniform in all the state compose the confederacy and moreover expressly provide that no preference shall be give by any regulation of commerce or revenue to the port of one state over those of another if the construction of a harbor or deepen the channel of a river be a regulation of commerce as the advocate of this power contend this would give the port of the state within which these improvement be make a preference over the port of other state and thus be a violation of the constitution it be not too much to assert that no human be in existence when the constitution be frame entertain the idea or the apprehension that by confer upon congress the power to regulate commerce its framer intend to embrace the power of construct road and canal and of create and improve harbor and deepen the channel of river throughout we extensive confederacy indeed one important branch of this very power have be deny to congress in express term by the convention a proposition be make in the convention to confer on congress the power to provide for the cutting of canal when deem necessary this be reject by the strong majority of eight state to three among the reason give for this rejection be that the expense in such case will fall on the united state and the benefit accrue to the place where the canal may be cut to say that the simple power of regulate commerce embrace within itself that of construct harbor of deepen the channel of river -- in short of create a system of internal improvement for the purpose of facilitate the operation of commerce -- would be to adopt a latitude of construction under which all political power might be usurp by the federal government such a construction would be in conflict with the well-known jealousy against federal power which actuate the framer of the constitution it be certain that the power in question be not enumerate among the express grant to congress contain in the instrument in construe the constitution we must then next inquire be its exercise necessary and proper -- not whether it may be convenient or useful for carry into execution the power to regulate commerce among the state but the jealous patriot of that day be not content even with this strict rule of construction apprehend that a dangerous latitude of interpretation might be apply in future time to the enumerated grant of power they procure a amendment to be make to the original instrument which declare that the power not delegate to the united state by the constitution nor prohibit by it to the state be reserve to the state respectively or to the people the distinctive spirit and character which pervade the constitution be that the power of the general government be confine chiefly to we intercourse with foreign nation to question of peace and war and to subject of common interest to all the state carefully leave the internal and domestic concern of each individual state to be control by its own people and legislature without specifically enumerate these power it must be admit that this well-marked distinction run through the whole instrument in nothing do the wisdom of its framer appear more conspicuously than in the care with which they seek to avoid the danger to we institution which must necessarily result from the interference of the federal government with the local concern of the state the jarring and collision which would occur from the exercise by two separate government of jurisdiction over the same subject could not fail to produce disastrous consequence besides the corrupting and seduce money influence exert by the general government in carry into effect a system of internal improvement might be pervert to increase and consolidate its own power to the detriment of the rights of the state if the power exist in congress to pass the present bill then tax must be impose and money borrow to a unlimited extent to carry such a system into execution equality among the state be equity this equality be the very essence of the constitution no preference can justly be give to one of the sovereign state over another accord to the best estimate we immense coast on the atlantic the gulf of mexico the pacific and the ivake embrace more than 9500 mile and measure by its indentation and to the head of tide water on the river the distance be believe to be more than 33000 mile this everywhere throughout its vast extent contain numerous river and harbor all of which may become the object of congressional appropriation you can not deny to one state what you have grant to another such injustice would produce strife jealousy and alarming dissension among they even within the same state improvement may be make in one river especial benefit of corporation or individual in they vicinity though they may have a odor of nationality on the principle that whatever benefit any part indirectly benefit the whole from we past history we may have a small foretaste of the cost of revive the system of internal improvement for more than thirty year after the adoption of the federal constitution the power to appropriate money a general system should be adopt which would make some approach to justice among all the state if this be possible what a vast field would the exercise of this power open for job and corruption member of congress from a honest desire to promote the interest of they constituent would struggle for improvement within they own district and the body itself must necessarily be convert into a arena where each would endeavor to obtain from the treasury as much money as possible for he own locality the temptation would prove irresistible a system of _ logrolling _ -lrb- i know no word so expressive michigan shall cease to depend on the treasury of the united state i doubt not that she in conjunction with upper canada will provide the necessary means for keep this work in repair in the least expensive and most effective manner and without be burdensome to any interest it have be contend in favor of the existence of the power to construct internal improvement that congress have from the bill entitle a act to secure homestead to actual settler on the public domain and for other purpose present to I on the 20th instant this bill give to every citizen of the united state who be the head acre and will from time to time transfer to they large body of such land which from peculiar circumstance may not be absorb by private purchase and settlement to the actual settler this bill do not reduce to about 18 cent per acre or one-seventh of the present minimum price of the public land in regard to the state it be a absolute and unqualified gift 1 this state of the fact raise the question whether congress under the constitution have the power to give away the public land either to state or individual on this question i express a decide opinion in my message to the house of representative of the 24th February 1859 return the agricultural-college bill this opinion remain unchanged the argument then use apply as a constitutional objection with greater force to the present bill _ there _ it have the plea of consideration grow out of a specific beneficial purpose _ here _ it be a absolute gratuity to the state without the pretext of consideration i be compel for want of time in these the last hour of the session to quote largely from this message i presume the general proposition will be admit that congress do not possess the power to make donation of money already in the treasury raise by tax on the people either to state or individual but it be contend that the public land be place upon a different footing from money raise by taxation and that the proceeds arise from they sale be not subject to the limitation of the constitution but may be appropriate or give away by congress at its own discretion to state corporation or individual for any purpose they may deem expedient the advocate of this bill attempt to sustain they position upon the language of the second clause of the third section of the fourth article of the constitution which declare that the congress shall have power to dispose of and make all needful rule and regulation respect the territory or other property belong to the united state they contend that by a fair interpretation of the word dispose of in this clause congress possess the power to make this gift of public land to the state for purpose of education it would require clear and strong evidence to induce the belief that the framer of the constitution after have limit the power of congress to certain precise and specific object intend by employ the word dispose of to give that body unlimited power over the vast public domain it would be a strange anomaly indeed to have create two fund -- the one by taxation confine to the execution of the enumerated power delegate to congress and the other from the public land applicable to all subject foreign and domestic which congress might designate that this fund should be dispose of not to pay the debt of the united state nor to raise and support army nor to provide and maintain a navy nor to accomplish any one of the other great object enumerate in the constitution but be divert from they to pay the debt of the state to educate they people and to carry into effect any other measure of they domestic policy this would be to confer upon congress a vast and irresponsible authority utterly at war with the well-known jealousy of federal power which prevail at the formation of the constitution the natural intendment would be that as the constitution confine congress to well-defined specific power the fund place at they command whether in land or money should be appropriate to the performance of the duty correspond with these power if not a government have be create with all its other power carefully limited but without any limitation in respect to the public land but i can not so read the word dispose of as to make they embrace the idea of give away the true meaning of word be always to be ascertain by the subject to which they be apply and the known general intent of the lawgiver congress be a trustee under the constitution for the people of the united state to dispose of they public land and i think i may venture to assert with confidence that no case can be find in which a trustee in the position of congress have be authorize to _ dispose of _ property by its owner where it have be hold that these word authorize such trustee to give away the fund intrust to he care no trustee when call upon to account for the disposition of the property place under he management before any judicial tribunal would venture to present such a plea in he defense the true meaning of these word be clearly state by chief justice taney in deliver the opinion of the court -lrb- 19 howard p 436 -rrb- he say in reference to this clause of the constitution : it begin its enumeration of power by that of dispose in other word make sale of the land or raise money from they which as we have already say be the main object of the cession -lrb- from the state -rrb- and which be the first thing provide for in the article it be unnecessary to refer to the history of the time to establish the known fact that this statement of the chief justice be perfectly well found that it never be intend by the framer of the constitution that these land should be give away by congress be manifest from the conclude portion of the same clause by it congress have power not only to dispose of the territory but of the other property of the united state in the language of the chief justice -lrb- p 437 -rrb- : and the same power of make needful rule respect the territory be in precisely the same language apply to the other property of the united state associate the power over the territory in this respect with the power over movable or personal property that be the ship arm or munitions of war which then belong in common to the state sovereignty the question be still clearer in regard to the public land in the state and territory within the louisiana and florida purchase these land be pay for out of the public treasury from money raise by taxation now if congress have no power to appropriate the money with which these land be purchase be it not clear that the power over the land be equally limit the mere conversion of this money into land could not confer upon congress new power over the disposition of land which they have not possess over money if it could then a trustee by change the character of the fund intrust to he care for special object from money into land might give the land away or devote it to any purpose he think proper however foreign from the trust the inference be irresistible that this land partake of the very same character with the money pay for it and can be devote to no object different from
