those pernicious social theory which have prove so disastrous in other country jame buchanan protest washington _ march 28 1860 _ _ to the house of representative _ : after a delay which have afford I ample time for reflection and after much and careful deliberation i find myself constrain by a imperious sense of duty as a coordinate branch of the federal government to protest against the first two clause of the first resolution adopt by the house of representative on the 5th instant and publish in the congressional globe on the succeed day these clause be in the follow word : _ resolve _ that a committee of five member be appoint by the speaker for the purpose first of investigate whether the president of the united state or any other officer of the government have by money patronage or other improper means seek to influence the action of congress or any committee thereof for or against the passage of any law appertaining to the rights of any state or territory and second also to inquire into and investigate whether any officer or officer of the government have by combination or otherwise prevent or defeat or attempt to prevent or defeat the execution of any law or law now upon the statute book and whether the president have fail or refuse to compel the execution of any law thereof i confine myself exclusively to these two branch of the resolution because the portion of it which follow relate to allege abuse in post-offices navy-yard public building and other public work of the united state in such case inquiry be highly proper in themselves and belong equally to the eighty-fourth jame buchanan by the president : lewi cass _ secretary of state _ fourth annual message washington city _ December 3 1860 _ _ fellow-citizen of the senate and house of representative _ : throughout the year since we last meeting the country have be eminently prosperous in all its material interest the general health have be excellent we harvest have be abundant and plenty smile throughout the land we commerce and manufacture have be prosecute with energy and industry and have yield fair and ample return in short no nation in the tide of time have ever present a spectacle of greater material prosperity than we have do until within a very recent period why be it then that discontent now so extensively prevail and the union of the state which be the source of all these blessing be threaten with destruction the long-continued and intemperate interference of the northern people with the question of slavery in the southern state have at length produce its natural effect the different section of the union be now array against each other and the time have arrive so much dread by the father of he country when hostile geographical party have be form i have long foresee and often forewarned my countryman of the now impending danger this do not proceed solely from the claim on the part of congress or the territorial legislature to exclude slavery from the territory nor from the effort of different state to defeat the execution of the fugitive-slave law all or any of these evil might have be endure by the south without danger to the union -lrb- as other have be -rrb- in the hope that time and reflection might apply the remedy the immediate peril arise not so much from these cause as from the fact that the incessant and violent agitation of the slavery question throughout the north for the last quarter of a century have at length produce its malign influence on the slave and inspire they with vague notion of freedom hence a sense of security no longer exist around the family altar this feeling of peace at home have give place to apprehension of servile insurrection many a matron throughout the south retire at night in dread of what may befall herself and child before the morning should this apprehension of domestic danger whether real or imaginary extend and intensify itself until it shall pervade the mass of the southern people then disunion will become inevitable self-preservation be the first law of nature and have be implant in the heart of man by he creator for the wisest purpose and no political union however fraught with blessing and benefit in all other respects can long continue if the necessary consequence be to render the home and the fireside of nearly half the party to it habitually and hopelessly insecure sooner or later the bond of such a union must be sever it be my conviction that this fatal period have not yet arrive and my prayer to god be that he would preserve the constitution and the union throughout all generation but let we take warning in time and remove the cause of danger it can not be deny that for five and twenty year the agitation at the north against slavery have be incessant in 1835 pictorial handbill and inflammatory appeal be circulate extensively throughout the south of a character to excite the passion of the slave and in the language of general jackson to stimulate they to insurrection and produce all the horror of a servile war this agitation have ever since be continue by the public press by the proceedings of state and county convention and by abolition sermon and lecture the time of congress have be occupy in violent speech on this never-ending subject and appeal in pamphlet and other form indorse by distinguished name have be send forth from this central point and spread broadcast over the union how easy would it be for the american people to settle the slavery question forever and to restore peace and harmony to this distract country they and they alone can do it all that be necessary to accomplish the object and all for which the slave state have ever contend be to be let alone and permit to manage they domestic institution in they own way as sovereign state they and they alone be responsible before god and the world for the slavery exist among they for this the people of the north be not more responsible and have no more right to interfere than with similar institution in russium or in brazil upon they good sense and patriotic forbearance i confess i still greatly rely without they aid it be beyond the power of any president no matter what may be he own political proclivity to restore peace and harmony among the state wisely limit and restrain as be he power under we constitution and law he alone can accomplish but little for good or for evil on such a momentous question and this bring I to observe that the election of any one of we fellow-citizen to the office of president do not of itself afford just cause for dissolve the union this be more especially true if he election have be effect by a mere plurality and not a majority of the people and have result from transient and temporary cause which may probably never again occur in order to justify a resort to revolutionary resistance the federal government must be guilty of a deliberate palpable and dangerous exercise of power not grant by the constitution the late presidential election however have be hold in strict conformity with its express provision how then can the result justify a revolution to destroy this very constitution reason justice a regard for the constitution all require that we shall wait for some overt and dangerous act on the part of the president elect before resort to such a remedy it be say however that the antecedent of the president elect have be sufficient to justify the fear of the south that he will attempt to invade they constitutional rights but be such apprehension of contingent danger in the future sufficient to justify the immediate destruction of the noblest system of government ever devise by mortal from the very nature of he office and its high responsibility he must necessarily be conservative the stern duty of administer the vast and complicated concern of this government afford in itself a guaranty that he will not attempt any violation of a clear constitutional right after all he be no more than the chief executive officer of the government he province be not to make but to execute the law and it be a remarkable fact in we history that notwithstanding the repeat effort of the antislavery party no single act have ever pass congress unless we may possibly except the missourus compromise impair in the slightest degree the rights of the south to they property in slave and it may also be observe judge from present indication that no probability exist of the passage of such a act by a majority of both house either in the present or the next congress surely under these circumstance we ought to be restrain from present action by the precept of he who speak as man never speak that sufficient unto the day be the evil thereof the day of evil may never come unless we shall rashly bring it upon ourselves it be allege as one cause for immediate secession that the southern state be deny equal rights with the other state in the common territory but by what authority be these deny not by congress which have never pass and i believe never will pass any act to exclude slavery from these territory and certainly not by the supreme court which have solemnly decide that slave be property and like all other property they owner have a right to take they into the common territory and hold they there under the protection of the constitution so far then as congress be concern the objection be not to anything they have already do but to what they may do hereafter it will surely be admit that this apprehension of future danger be no good reason for a immediate dissolution of the union it be true that the territorial legislature of kansa on the 23d February 1860 pass in great haste a act over the veto of the governor declare that slavery be and shall be forever prohibit in this territory such a act however plainly violate the rights of property secure by the constitution will surely be declare void by the judiciary whenever it shall be present in a legal form only three day after my inauguration the supreme court of the united state solemnly adjudge that this power do not exist in a territorial legislature yet such have be the factious temper of the time that the correctness of this decision have be extensively impugn before the people and the question have give rise to angry political conflict throughout the country those who have appeal from this judgment of we highest constitutional tribunal to popular assembly would if they could invest a territorial legislature with power to annul the sacred rights of property this power congress be expressly forbid by the federal constitution to exercise every state legislature in the union be forbid by its own constitution to exercise it it can not be exercise in any state except by the people in they highest sovereign capacity when frame or amend they state constitution in like manner it can only be exercise by the people of a territory represent in a convention of delegate for the purpose of frame a constitution preparatory to admission as a state into the union then and not until then be they invest with power to decide the question whether slavery shall or shall not exist within they limit this be a act of sovereign authority and not of subordinate territorial legislation be it otherwise then indeed would the equality of the state in the territory be destroy and the rights of property in slave would depend not upon the guaranty of the constitution but upon the shift majority of a irresponsible territorial legislature such a doctrine from its intrinsic unsoundness can not long influence any considerable portion of we people much less can it afford a good reason for a dissolution of the union the most palpable violation of constitutional duty which have yet be commit consist in the act of different state legislature to defeat the execution of the fugitive-slave law it ought to be remembered however that for these act neither congress nor any president can justly be hold responsible have be pass in violation of the federal constitution they be therefore null and void all the court both state and national before whom the question have arise have from the beginning declare the fugitive-slave law to be constitutional the single exception be that of a state court in wisconsin and this have not only be reverse by the proper appellate tribunal but have meet with such universal reprobation that there can be no danger from it as a precedent the validity of this law have be establish over and over again by the supreme court of the united state with perfect it be a well-known historical fact that the constitution itself could never have be adopt by the convention in one form or other under the act of 1793 and 1850 both be substantially the same the own to act with vigor in execute this supreme law against the conflict enactment of state legislature should he fail in the performance of this high duty he will then have manifest a disregard of the constitution and law to the great injury of the people of nearly one-half of the state of the union but be we to presume in advance that he will thus violate he duty this would be at war with every principle of justice and of christian charity let we wait for the overt act the fugitive-slave law have be carry into execution in every contest case since the commencement of the present administration though often it be to be regret with great loss and inconvenience to the master and with considerable expense to the government let we trust that the state legislature will repeal they unconstitutional and obnoxious enactment unless this shall be do without unnecessary delay it be impossible for any human power to save the union the southern state stand on the basis of the constitution have a right to demand this act of justice from the state of the north should it be refuse then the constitution to which all the state be party will have be willfully violate by one portion of they in a provision essential to the domestic security and happiness of the remainder in that event the injured state after have first use all peaceful and constitutional means to obtain redress would be justify in revolutionary resistance to the government of the union i have purposely confine my remark to revolutionary resistance because it have be claim within the last few year that any state whenever this shall be its sovereign will and pleasure may secede from the union in accordance with the constitution and without any violation of the constitutional rights of the other member of the confederacy that as each become party to the union by the vote of its own people assemble in convention so any one of they may retire from the union in a similar manner by the vote of such a convention in order to justify secession as a constitutional remedy it must be on the principle that the federal government be a mere voluntary association of state to be dissolve at pleasure by any one of the contracting party if this be so the confederacy be a rope of sand to be penetrate and dissolve by the first adverse wave of public opinion in any of the state in this manner we thirty-three state may resolve themselves into as many petty jarring and hostile republic each one retire from the union without responsibility whenever any sudden excitement might impel they to such a course by this process a union might be entirely break into fragment in a few week which cost we forefather many year of toil privation and blood to establish such a principle be wholly inconsistent with the history as well as the character of the federal constitution after it be frame with the greatest deliberation and care it be submit to convention of the people of the several state for ratification its provision be discuss at length in these body compose of the first man of the country its opponent contend that it confer power upon the federal government dangerous to the rights of the state whilst its advocate maintain that under a fair construction of the instrument there be no foundation for such apprehension in that mighty struggle between the first intellect of this or any other country it never occur to any individual either among its opponent or advocate to assert or even to intimate that they effort be all vain labor because the moment that any state feel herself aggrieve she might secede from the union what a crush argument would this have prove against those who dread that the rights of the state would be endanger by the constitution the truth be that it be the 16th of January 1833 transmit the nullify ordinance of south carolina to congress employ the follow language : the right of the people of a single state to absolve themselves at will and without -- it be form by the state that be by the people in each of the state act in they highest sovereign capacity and form consequently by the same authority which form the state constitution nor be the be within they several sphere it be like they organize into legislative executive and judiciary department it operate like they directly on person and thing and like they it have at command a physical union shall be perpetual the preamble to the constitution of the united state have express reference to the article of confederation recite that it be establish in order to form a more perfect union and yet it be contend that this more perfect union do not include the essential attribute of perpetuity but that the union be design to be perpetual appear conclusively from the nature and extent of the power confer by the constitution on the federal government these power embrace the very highest attribute of national sovereignty they place both the sword and the purse under its control congress have power to make war and to make peace to raise and support army and navy and to conclude treaty with foreign government it be invest with the power to coin money and to regulate the value thereof and to regulate commerce with foreign nation and among the several state it be not necessary to enumerate the other high power which have be confer upon the federal government in order to carry the enumerated power into effect congress possess the exclusive right to lay and collect duty on import and in common with the state to lay and collect all other tax but the constitution have not only confer these high power upon congress but it have adopt effectual means to restrain the state from interfere with they exercise for that purpose it have in strong prohibitory language expressly declare that -- no state shall enter into any treaty alliance or confederation grant letter of marque and reprisal coin money emit bill of credit make anything but gold and silver coin a tender in payment of debt pass any bill of attainder _ ex post facto _ law or law impair the obligation of contract moreover -- no state shall without the consent of the congress lay any impost or duty on import or export except what may be absolutely necessary for execute its inspection law and if they exceed this amount the excess shall belong to the united state and -- no state shall without the consent of congress lay any duty of tonnage keep troops or ship of war in time of peace enter into any agreement or compact with another state or with a foreign power or engage in war unless actually invade or in such imminent danger as will not admit of delay in order still further to secure the uninterrupted exercise of these high power against state interposition it be provide : that -- this constitution and the law of the united state which shall be make in pursuance thereof and all treaty make or which shall be make under the authority of the united state shall be the supreme law of the land and the judge in every state shall be bind thereby anything in the constitution or law of any state to the contrary notwithstanding the solemn sanction of religion have be superad to the obligation of official duty and all senator and representative of the united state all member of state legislature and all executive and judicial officer both of the united state and of the several state shall be bind by oath or affirmation to support this constitution in order to carry into effect these power the constitution have establish a perfect government in all its form -- legislative executive and judicial and this government to the extent of its power act directly upon the individual citizen of every state and execute its own decree by the agency of its own officer in this respect it differ entirely from the government under the old confederation which be confine to make requisition on the state in they sovereign character this leave it in the discretion of each whether to obey or to refuse and they often decline to comply with such requisition it thus become necessary for the purpose of remove this barrier and in order to form a more perfect union to establish a government which could act directly upon the people and execute its own law without the intermediate agency of the state this have be accomplish by the constitution of the united state in short the government create by the constitution and derive its authority from the sovereign people of each of the several state have precisely the same right to exercise its power over the people of all these state in the enumerated case that each one of they possess over subject not delegate to the united state but reserve to the state respectively or to the people to the extent of the delegated power the great and powerful government invest with all the attribute of sovereignty over the special subject to which its authority extend its framer never intend to implant in its bosom the seed of its own they do not fear nor have they any reason to imagine that the constitution would ever be so interpret as to enable any state by she own act and without the consent of she sister state to discharge she law of the united state to secure the administration of justice by means of the federal judiciary be concern all the federal officer within its limit through whose agency alone these law can be carry of brazil we relation continue to be of the most amicable character the exchange of the ratification of the convention with the republic of new granada sign at washington on the 10th of September 1857 convention the government of new granada have specially acknowledge itself to be responsible to we citizen for damages which be cause by the riot at panama on the 15th April 1856 these claim together with other claim of we citizen which have be long urge in vain be refer for adjustment to a board of commissioner i submit a copy of the convention to congress and recommend the legislation necessary to carry it into effect persevere effort have be make for the adjustment of the claim of american citizen against the government of costa rica and i be happy to inform you that these have finally prevail a convention be sign at the city of san jose on the 2d July last between the minister resident of the united state in costa rica and the plenipotentiary of that republic refer these claim to a board of commissioner and provide for the payment of they award this convention will be submit immediately to the senate for they constitutional action the claim of we citizen upon the republic of nicaragua have not yet be provide for by treaty although diligent effort for this purpose have be make by we minister resident to that republic these be still continue with a fair prospect of success we relation with mexico remain in a most unsatisfactory condition in my last two annual message i discuss extensively the subject of these relation and do not now propose to repeat at length the fact and argument then present they prove conclusively that we citizen reside in mexico and we merchant trade thereto have suffer a series of wrong and outrage such as we have never patiently bear from any other nation for these we successive minister invoke the faith of treaty have in the name of they country persistently demand redress and indemnification but without the slightest effect indeed so confident have the mexican authority become of we patient endurance that they universally believe they might commit these outrage upon american citizen with absolute impunity thus write we minister in 1856 and express the opinion that nothing but a manifestation of the power of the government and of its purpose to punish these wrong will avail afterwards in 1857 come the adoption of a new constitution for mexico the election of a president and congress under its provision and the inauguration of the president within one short month however this president be expel from the capital by a rebellion in the army and the supreme power of the republic be assign to general zuloaga this usurper be in he turn soon compel to retire and give place to general miramon under the constitution which have thus be adopt seor juarez as chief justice of the supreme court become the lawful president of the republic and it be for the maintenance of the constitution and he authority derive from it that the civil war commence and still continue to be prosecute throughout the year 1858 the constitutional party grow stronger and stronger in the previous history of mexico a successful military revolution at the capital have almost universally be the signal for submission throughout the republic not so on the present occasion a majority of the citizen persistently sustain the constitutional government when this be recognize in April 1859 by the government of the united state its authority extend over a large majority of the mexican state and people include vera cruz and all the other important seaport of the republic from that period we commerce with mexico begin to revive and the constitutional government have afford it all the protection in its power meanwhile the government of miramon still hold sway at the capital and over the surrounding country and continue its outrage against the few american citizen who still have the courage to remain within its power to cap the climax after the battle of tacubaya in April 1859 general marquez order three citizen of the united state two of they physician to be seize in the hospital at that place take out and shoot without crime and without trial this be do notwithstanding we unfortunate countryman be at the moment engage in the holy cause of afford relief to the soldier of both party who have be wound in the battle without make any distinction between they the time have arrive in my opinion when this government be bind to exert its power to avenge and redress the wrong of we citizen and to afford they protection in mexico the interpose obstacle be that the portion of the country under the sway of miramon could not be reach without pass over territory under the jurisdiction of the constitutional government under these circumstance i deem it my duty to recommend to congress in my last annual message the employment of a sufficient military force to penetrate into the interior where the government of miramon be to be find with or if need be without the consent of the juarez government though it be not doubt that this consent could be obtain never have i have a clearer conviction on any subject than of the justice as well as wisdom of such a policy no other alternative be leave except the entire abandonment of we fellow-citizen who have go to mexico under the faith of treaty to the systematic injustice cruelty and oppression of miramon 's government besides it be almost certain that the simple authority to employ this force would of itself have accomplish all we object without strike a single blow the constitutional government would then ere this have be establish at the city of mexico and would have be ready and willing to the extent of its ability to do we justice in addition -- and i deem this a most important consideration -- european government would have be deprive of all pretext to interfere in the territorial and domestic concern of mexico we should thus have be relieve from the obligation of resist even by force should this become necessary any attempt by these government to deprive we neighbor republic of portion of she territory -- a duty from which we could not shrink without abandon the traditional and established policy of the american people i be happy to observe that firmly rely upon the justice and good faith of these government there be no present danger that such a contingency will happen have discover that my recommendation would not be sustain by congress the next alternative be to accomplish in some degree if possible the same object by treaty stipulation with the constitutional government such treaty be accordingly conclude by we late able and excellent minister to mexico and on the 4th of January last be submit to the senate for ratification as these have not yet receive the final action of that body it would be improper for I to present a detailed statement of they provision still i may be permit to express the opinion in advance that they be calculate to promote the agricultural manufacturing and commercial interest of the country and to secure we just influence with a adjoining republic as to whose fortune and fate we can never feel indifferent whilst at the same time they provide for the payment of a considerable amount toward the satisfaction of the claim of we injured fellow-citizen at the period of my inauguration i be confront in kansa by a revolutionary government exist under what be call the topeka constitution its avowed object be to subdue the territorial government by force and to inaugurate what be call the topeka government in its stead to accomplish this object a extensive military organization be form and its command intrust to the most violent revolutionary leader under these circumstance it become my imperative duty to exert the whole constitutional power of the executive to prevent the flame of civil war from again rage in kansa which in the excited state of the public mind both north and south might have extend into the neighboring state the hostile party in kansa have be inflamed against each other by emissary both from the north and the south to a degree of malignity without parallel in we history to prevent actual collision and to assist the civil magistrate in enforce the law a strong detachment of the army be station in the territory ready to aid the marshal and he deputy when lawfully call upon as a _ posse comilatus _ in the execution of civil and criminal process still the trouble in kansa could not have be permanently settle without a election by the people the ballot box be the surest arbiter of dispute among freeman under this conviction every proper effort be employ to induce the hostile party to vote at the election of delegate to frame a state constitution and afterwards at the election to decide whether kansa should be a slave or free state the insurgent party refuse to vote at either lest this might be consider a recognition on they part of the territorial government establish by congress a better spirit however seem soon after to prevail and the two party meet face to face at the third election hold on the first Monday of January 1858 for member of the legislature and state officer under the lecompton constitution the result be the triumph of the antislavery party at the poll this decision of the ballot box prove clearly that this party be in the majority and remove the danger of civil war from that time we have hear little or nothing of the topeka government and all serious danger of revolutionary trouble in kansa be then at a end the lecompton constitution which have be thus recognize at this state election by the vote of both political party in kansa be transmit to I with the request that i should present it to congress this i could not have refuse to do without violate my clearest and strongest conviction of duty the constitution and all the proceedings which precede and follow its formation be fair and regular on they face i then believe and experience have prove that the interest of the people of kansa would have be best consult by its admission as a state into the union especially as the majority within a brief period could have amend the constitution accord to they will and pleasure if fraud exist in all or any of these proceedings it be not for the president but for congress to investigate and determine the question of fraud and what ought to be its consequence if at the first two election the majority refuse to vote it can not be pretend that this refusal to exercise the elective franchise could invalidate a election fairly hold under lawful authority even if they have not subsequently vote at the third election it be true that the whole constitution have not be submit to the people as i always desire but the precedent be numerous of the admission of state into the union without such submission it would not comport with my present purpose to review the proceedings of congress upon the lecompton constitution it be sufficient to observe that they final action have remove the last vestige of serious revolutionary trouble the desperate band recently assemble under a notorious outlaw in the southern portion of the territory to resist the execution of the law and to plunder peaceful citizen will i doubt not be speedily subdue and bring to justice have i treat the lecompton constitution as a nullity and refuse to transmit it to congress it be not difficult to imagine whilst recall the position of the country at that moment what would have be the disastrous consequence both in and out of the territory from such a dereliction of duty on the part of the executive peace have also be restore within the territory of utah which at the commencement of my administration be in a state of open rebellion this be the more dangerous as the people animated by a fanatical spirit and intrench within they distant mountain fastness might have make a long and formidable resistance cost what it might it be necessary to bring they into subjection to the constitution and the law sound policy therefore as well as humanity require that this object should if possible be accomplish without the effusion of blood this could only be effect by send a military force into the territory sufficiently strong to convince the people that resistance would be hopeless and at the same time to offer they a pardon for past offens on condition of immediate submission to the government this policy be pursue with eminent success and the only cause for regret be the heavy expenditure require to march a large detachment of the army to that remote region and to furnish it subsistence utah be now comparatively peaceful and quiet and the military force have be withdraw except that portion of it necessary to keep the indian in check and to protect the emigrant train on they way to we pacific possession in my first annual message i promise to employ my best exertion in cooperation with congress to reduce the expenditure of the government within the limit of a wise and judicious economy a overflow treasury have produce habit of prodigality and extravagance which could only be gradually correct the work require both time and patience i apply myself diligently to this task from the beginning and be aid by the able and energetic effort of the head of the different executive department the result of we labor in this good cause do not appear in the sum total of we expenditure for the first two year mainly in consequence of the extraordinary expenditure necessarily incur in the utah expedition and the very large amount of the contingent expense of congress during this period these greatly exceed the pay and mileage of the member for the year end June 30 1858 whilst the pay and mileage amount to $ 1490214 the contingent expense rise to $ 209330979 and for the year end June 30 1859 whilst the pay and mileage amount to $ 85909366 the contingent expense amount to $ 143156578 i be happy however to be able to inform you that during the last fiscal year end June 30 1860 the total expenditure of the government in all its branch -- legislative executive and judicial -- exclusive of the public debt be reduce to the sum of $ 5540246546 this conclusively appear from the book of the treasury in the year end June 30 1858 the total year end June 30 1860 include $ 104066771 for the contingent expense of congress there must be deduct from this amount the sum of $ 429600926 with the interest upon it of $ 150000 appropriate by the act of February 15 1860 for the purpose of supply the deficiency in the revenue and defray the expense of the post-office department for the year end June 30 1859 this sum therefore justly chargeable to the year 1859 must be deduct from the sum of $ 5984847472 in order to ascertain the expenditure for the year end June 30 1860 which leave a balance for the expenditure of that year of $ 5540246546 the interest on the public debt include treasury note for the same fiscal year end June 30 1860 amount to $ 317731462 which add to the above sum of $ 5540246546 make the aggregate of $ 5857978008 it ought in justice to be observe that several of the estimate from the department for the year end June 30 1860 be reduce by congress below what be and still be deem compatible with the public interest allow a liberal margin of $ 2500000 for this reduction and for other cause it may be safely assert that the sum of $ 61000000 or at the most $ 62000000 be amply sufficient to administer the government and to pay the interest on the public debt unless contingent event should hereafter render extraordinary expenditure necessary this result have be attain in a considerable degree by the care exercise by the appropriate department in enter into public contract i have myself never interfere with the award of any such contract except in a single case with the colonization society deem it advisable to cast the whole responsibility in each case on the proper head of the department with the general instruction that these contract should always be give to the lowest and best bidder it have ever be my opinion that public contract be not a legitimate source of patronage to be confer upon personal or political favorite but that in all such case a public officer be bind to act for the government as a prudent individual would act for himself it be with great satisfaction i communicate the fact that since the date of my last annual message not a single slave have be import into the united state in violation of the law prohibit the african slave trade this statement be found upon a thorough examination and investigation of the subject indeed the spirit which prevail some time since among a portion of we fellow-citizen in favor of this trade seem to have entirely subside i also congratulate you upon the public sentiment which now exist against the crime of set on foot military expedition within the limit of the united state to proceed from thence and make war upon the people of unoffending state with whom we be at peace in this respect a happy change have be effect since the commencement of my administration it surely ought to be the prayer of every christian and patriot that such expedition may never again receive countenance in we country or depart from we shore it would be a useless repetition to do more than refer with earnest commendation to my former recommendation in favor of the pacific railroad of the grant of power to the president to employ the naval force in the vicinity for the protection of the life and property of we fellow-citizen pass in transit over the different central american route against sudden and lawless outbreak and depredation and also to protect american merchant vessel they crew and cargo against violent and unlawful seizure and confiscation in the port of mexico and the south american republic when these may be in a disturbed and revolutionary condition it be my settled conviction that without such a power we do not afford that protection to those engage in the commerce of the country which they have a right to demand i again recommend to congress the passage of a law in pursuance of the provision of the constitution appoint a day certain previous to the 4th march in each year of a odd number for the election of representative throughout all the state a similar power have already be exercise with general approbation in the appointment of the same day throughout the union for hold the election of elector for president and vice-president of the united state my attention be earnestly direct to this subject from the fact that the thirty-fifth congress terminate on the 3d march 1859 without make the necessary appropriation for the service of the post-office department i be then force to consider the best remedy for this omission and a immediate call of the present congress be the natural resort upon inquiry however i ascertain that fifteen out of the thirty-three state compose the confederacy be without representative and that consequently these fifteen state would be disfranchise by such a call these fifteen state will be in the same condition on the 4th march next ten of they can not elect representative accord to exist state law until different period extend from the beginning of August next until the month of October and November in my last message i give warn that in a time of sudden and alarming danger the salvation of we institution might depend upon the power of the president immediately to assemble a full congress to meet the emergency it be now quite evident that the financial necessity of the government will require a modification of the tariff during you present session for the purpose of increase the revenue in this aspect i desire to reiterate the recommendation contain in my last two annual message in favor of impose specific instead of _ ad valorem _ duty on all import article to which these can be properly apply from long observation and experience i be convince that specific duty be necessary both to protect the revenue and to secure to we manufacturing interest that amount of incidental encouragement which unavoidably result from a revenue tariff as a abstract proposition it may be admit that _ ad valorem _ duty would in theory be the most just and equal but if the experience of this and of all other commercial nation have demonstrate that such duty can not be assess and collect without great fraud upon the revenue then it be the part of wisdom to resort to specific duty indeed from the very nature of a _ ad valorem _ duty this must be the result under it the inevitable consequence be that foreign goods will be enter at less than they true value the treasury will therefore lose the duty on the difference between they real and fictitious value and to this extent we be defraud the temptation which _ ad valorem _ duty present to a dishonest importer be irresistible he object be to pass he goods through the custom-house at the very lowest valuation necessary to save they from confiscation in this he too often succeed in spite of the vigilance of the revenue officer hence the resort to false invoice one for the purchaser and another for the custom-house and to other expedient to defraud the government the honest importer produce he invoice to the collector state the actual price at which he purchase the article abroad not so the dishonest importer and the agent of the foreign manufacturer and here it may be observe that a very large proportion of the manufacture import from abroad be consign for sale to commission merchant who be mere agent employ by the manufacturer in such case no actual sale have be make to fix they value the foreign manufacturer if he be dishonest prepare a invoice of the goods not at they actual value but at the very lowest rate necessary to escape detection in this manner the dishonest importer and the foreign manufacturer enjoy a decide advantage over the honest merchant they be thus enable to undersell the fair trader and drive he from the market in fact the operation of this system have already drive from the pursuit of honorable commerce many of that class of regular and conscientious merchant whose character throughout the world be the pride of we country the remedy for these evil be to be find in specific duty so far as this may be practicable they dispense with any inquiry at the custom-house into the actual cost or value of the article and it pay the precise amount of duty previously fix by law they present no temptation to the appraiser of foreign goods who receive but small salary and might by undervaluation in a few case render themselves independent besides specific duty best conform to the requisition in the constitution that no preference shall be give by any regulation of commerce or revenue to the port of one state over those of another under we _ ad valorem _ system such preference be to some extent inevitable and complaint have often be make that the spirit of this provision have be violate by a lower appraisement of the same article at one port than at another a impression strangely enough prevail to some extent that specific duty be necessarily protective duty nothing can be more fallacious great britain glory in free trade and yet she whole revenue from import be at the present moment collect under a system of specific duty it be a striking fact in this connection that in the commercial treaty of January 23 1860 between france and england one of the article provide that the _ ad valorem _ duty which it impose shall be convert into specific duty within six month from its date and these be to be ascertain by make a average of the price for six month previous to that time the reverse of the proposition would be nearer to the truth because a much larger amount of revenue would be collect by merely convert the _ ad valorem _ duty of a tariff into equivalent specific duty to this extent the revenue would be increase and in the same proportion the specific duty might be diminish specific duty would secure to the american manufacturer the incidental protection to which he be fairly entitle under a revenue tariff and to this surely no person would object the framer of the exist tariff have go further and in a liberal spirit have discriminate in favor of large and useful branch of we manufacture not by raise the rate of duty upon the importation of similar article from abroad but what be the same in effect by admit article free of duty which enter into the composition of they fabric under the present system it have be often truly remark that this incidental protection decrease when the manufacturer need it most and increase when he need it least and constitute a slide scale which always operate against he the revenue of the country be subject to similar fluctuation instead of approach a steady standard as would be the case under a system of specific duty they sink and rise with the sinking and rise price of article in foreign country it would not be difficult for congress to arrange a system of specific duty which would afford additional stability both to we revenue and we manufacture and without injury or injustice to any interest of the country this might be accomplish by ascertain the average value of any give article for a series of year at the place of exportation and by simply convert the rate of _ ad valorem _ duty upon it which might be deem necessary for revenue purpose into the form of a specific duty such a arrangement could not injure the consumer if he should pay a greater amount of duty one year this would be counterbalance by a lesser amount the next and in the end the aggregate would be the same i desire to call you immediate attention to the present condition of the treasury so ably and clearly present by the secretary in he report to congress and to recommend that measure be promptly adopt to enable it to discharge its press obligation the other recommendation of the report be well worthy of you favorable consideration i herewith transmit to congress the report of the secretary of war of the navy of the interior and of the postmaster-general the recommendation and suggestion which they contain be highly valuable and deserve you careful attention the report of the postmaster-general detail the circumstance under which cornelius vanderbilt on my request agree in the month of July last to carry the ocean mail between we atlantic and pacific coast have he not thus act this important intercommunication must have be suspend at least for a season the postmaster-general have no power to make he any other compensation than the postage on the mail matter which he might carry it be know at the time that these postage would fall far short of a adequate compensation as well as of the sum which the same service have previously cost the government mr vanderbilt in a commendable spirit be willing to rely upon the justice of congress to make up the deficiency and i therefore recommend that a appropriation may be grant for this purpose i should do great injustice to the attorney-general be i to omit the mention of he distinguished service in the measure adopt and prosecute by he for the defense of the government against numerous and unfounded claim to land in californium purport to have be make by the mexican government previous to the treaty of cession the successful opposition to these claim have save the united state public property worth many million of dollar and to individual hold title under they to at least a equal amount it have be represent to I from source which i deem reliable that the inhabitant in several portion of kansa have be reduce nearly to a state of starvation on account of the almost total failure of they crop whilst the harvest in every other portion of the country have be abundant the prospect before they for the approach winter be well calculate to enlist the sympathy of every heart the destitution appear to be so general that it can not be relieve by private contribution and they be in such indigent circumstance as to be unable to purchase the necessaries of life for themselves i refer the subject to congress if any constitutional measure for they relief can be devise i would recommend its adoption i cordially commend to you favorable regard the interest of the people of this district they be eminently entitle to you consideration especially since unlike the people of the state they can appeal to no government except that of the union jame buchanan special message washington _ December 5 1860 _ _ to the senate of washington city _ January 8 1861 _ _ to the senate and house of representative _ : at the opening of you present session i call you attention to the danger which threaten the existence of the union i express my opinion freely concern the original cause of those danger and recommend such measure as i believe would have the effect of tranquilize the country and save it from the peril in which it have be needlessly and most unfortunately involve those opinion and recommendation i do not propose now to repeat my own conviction upon the whole subject remain unchanged the fact that a great calamity be impend over the nation be even at that time acknowledge by every intelligent citizen it have already make itself feel throughout the length and breadth of the land the necessary consequence of the alarm thus produce be most deplorable the import fall off with a rapidity never know before except in time of war in the history of we foreign commerce the treasury be unexpectedly leave without the means which it have reasonably count upon to meet the public engagement trade be paralyzed manufacture be stop the best public security suddenly sink in the market every species of property depreciate more or less and thousand of poor man who depend upon they daily labor for they daily bread be turn out of employment i deeply regret that i be not able to give you any information upon the state of the union which be more satisfactory than what i be then oblige to communicate on the contrary matter be still worse at present than they then be when congress meet a strong hope pervade the whole public mind that some amicable adjustment of the subject would speedily be make by the representative of the state and of the people which might restore peace between the conflicting section of the country that hope have be diminish by every hour of delay and as the prospect of a bloodless settlement fade away the public distress become more and more aggravate as evidence of this it be only necessary to say that the treasury note authorize by the act of 17th of December last be advertise accord to the law and that no responsible bidder offer to take any considerable sum at par at a lower rate of interest than 12 per cent from these fact it appear that in a government organize like ours domestic strife or even a well-grounded fear of civil hostility be more destructive to we public and private interest than the most formidable foreign war in my annual message i express the conviction which i have long deliberately hold and which recent reflection have only tend to deepen and confirm that no state have a right by its own act to secede from the union or throw off its federal obligation at pleasure i also declare my opinion to be that even if that right exist and should be exercise by any state of the confederacy the executive department of this government have no authority under the constitution to recognize its validity by acknowledge the independence of such state this leave I no alternative as the chief executive officer under the constitution of the united state but to collect the public revenue and to protect the public property so far as this might be practicable under exist law this be still my purpose my province be to execute and not to make the law it belong to congress exclusively to repeal to modify or to enlarge they provision to meet exigency as they may occur i possess no dispense power i certainly have no right to make aggressive war upon any state and i be perfectly satisfy that the constitution have wisely withhold that power even from congress but the right and the duty to use military force defensively against those who resist the federal officer in the execution of they legal function and against those who assail the property of the federal government be clear and undeniable but the dangerous and hostile attitude of the state toward each other have already far transcend and cast in the shade the ordinary executive duty already provide for by law and have assume such vast and alarming proportion as to place the subject entirely above and beyond executive control the fact can not be disguise that we be in the midst of a great revolution in all its various bearing therefore i commend the question to congress as the only human tribunal under providence possess the power to meet the exist emergency to they exclusively belong the power to declare war or to authorize the employment of military force in all case contemplate by the constitution and they alone possess the power to remove grievance which might lead to war and to secure peace and union to this distract country on they and on they alone rest the responsibility the union be a sacred trust leave by we revolutionary father to they descendant and never do any other people inherit so rich a legacy it have render we prosperous in peace and triumphant in war the national flag have float in glory over every sea under its shadow american citizen have find protection and respect in all land beneath the sun if we descend to consideration of purely material interest when in the history of all time have a confederacy be bind together by such strong tie of mutual interest each portion of it be dependent on all and all upon each portion for prosperity and domestic security free trade throughout the whole supplies the want of one portion from the production of another and scatter wealth everywhere the great planting and farming state require the aid of the commercial and navigating state to send they production to domestic and foreign market and to furnish the naval power to render they transportation secure against all hostile attack should the union perish in the midst of the present excitement we have already have a sad foretaste of the universal suffering which would result from its destruction the calamity would be severe in every portion of the union and would be quite as great to say the least in the southern as in the northern state the greatest aggravation of the evil and that which would place we in the most unfavorable light both before the world and posterity be as i be firmly convince that the secession movement have be chiefly base upon a misapprehension at the south of the sentiment of the majority in several of the northern state let the question be transfer from political assembly to the ballot box and the people themselves would speedily redress the serious grievance which the south have suffer but in heaven 's name let the trial be make before we plunge into armed conflict upon the mere assumption that there be no other alternative time be a great conservative power let we pause at this momentous point and afford the people both north and south a opportunity for reflection would that south carolina have be convince of this truth before she precipitate action i therefore appeal through you to the people of the country to declare in they might that the union must and shall be preserve by all constitutional means i most earnestly recommend that you devote yourselve exclusively to the question how this can be accomplish in peace all other question when compare to this sink into insignificance the present be no time for palliation action prompt action be require a delay in congress to prescribe or to recommend a distinct and practical proposition for conciliation may drive we to a point from which it will be almost impossible to recede a common ground on which conciliation and harmony can be produce be surely not unattainable the proposition to compromise by let the north have exclusive control of the territory above a certain line and to give southern institution protection below that line ought to receive universal approbation in itself indeed it may not be entirely satisfactory but when the alternative be between a reasonable concession on both side and a destruction of the union it be a imputation upon the patriotism of congress to assert that its member will hesitate for a moment even now the danger be upon we in several of the state which have not yet secede the fort arsenal and magazine of the united state have be seize this be by far the most serious step which have be take since the commencement of the trouble this public property have long be leave without garrison and troops for its protection because no person doubt its security under the flag of the country in any state of the union besides we small army have scarcely be sufficient to guard we remote frontier against indian incursion the seizure of this property from all appearance have be purely aggressive and not in resistance to any attempt to coerce a state or state to remain in the union at the beginning of these unhappy trouble i determine that no act of mine should increase the excitement in either section of the country if the political conflict be to end in a civil war it be my determine purpose not to commence it nor even to furnish a excuse for it by any act of this government my opinion remain unchanged that justice as well as sound policy require we still to seek a peaceful solution of the question at issue between the north and the south entertaining this conviction i refrain even from send reenforcement to major anderson who command the fort in charleston harbor until a absolute necessity for do so should make itself apparent lest it might unjustly be regard as a menace of military coercion and thus furnish if not a provocation at least a pretext for a outbreak on the part of south carolina no necessity for these reenforcement seem to exist i be assure by distinguished and upright gentleman of south carolina that no attack upon major anderson be intend but that on the contrary it be the desire of the state authority as much as it be my own to avoid the fatal consequence which must eventually follow a military collision and here i deem it proper to submit for you information copy of a department have be perform by mr holt from the day last mention to the present time the power to carry on the business of the government by means of a provisional appointment when a vacancy occur be expressly give by the act of February 13 1795 which enact -- that in case of vacancy in the office of secretary of state secretary of the treasury or of the secretary of the department of war or of any officer of either of the say department whose appointment be not in the head thereof whereby they can not perform the duty of they respective office it shall be lawful for the president of the united state in case he shall think it necessary to authorize any person or person at he discretion to perform the duty of the say respective office until a successor be appoint or such vacancy be fill : _ provide _ that no one vacancy shall be supply in manner aforesaid for a longer period than six month it be manifest that if the power which this law give have be withhold the public interest would frequently suffer very serious detriment vacancy may occur at any time in the most important office which can not be immediately and permanently fill in a manner satisfactory to the appoint power it be wise to make a provision which would enable the president to avoid a total suspension of business in the interval and equally wise so to limit the executive discretion as to prevent any serious abuse of it this be what the framer of the act of 1795 do and neither the policy nor the constitutional validity of they law have be question for sixty-five year the practice of make such appointment whether in a vacation or during the session of congress have be constantly follow during every administration from the earliest period of the government and its perfect lawfulness have never to my knowledge be question or deny without go back further than the year 1829 and without take into the calculation any but the chief officer of the several department it will be find that provisional appointment to fill vacancy be make to the number of 179 from the commencement of general jackson 's administration to the close of general pierce 's this number would probably be greatly increase if all the case which occur in the subordinate office and bureau be add to the count some of they be make while the senate be in session some which be make in vacation be continue in force long after the senate assemble sometimes the temporary officer be the commission head of another department sometimes a subordinate in the same department sometimes the affair of the navy department have be direct _ ad interim _ by a commodore and those of the war department by a general in most if not all of the case which occur previous to 1852 it be believe that the compensation provide by law for the officer regularly commission be pay to the person who discharge the duty _ ad interim _ to give the senate a more detailed and satisfactory view of the subject i send the accompany tabular statement certify by the secretary of state in which the instance be all set forth in which provisional as well as permanent appointment be make to the highest executive office from 1829 nearly to the present time with they respective date it must be allow that these precedent so numerous and so long continue be entitle to great respect since we can scarcely suppose that the wise and eminent man by whom they be make could have be mistake on a point which be bring to they attention so often still less can it be suppose that any of they willfully violate the law or the constitution the lawfulness of the practice rest upon the exigency of the public service which require that the movement of the government shall not be arrest by a accidental vacancy in one of the department upon a act of congress expressly and plainly give and regulate the power and upon long and uninterrupted usage of the executive which have never be challenge as illegal by congress this answer the inquiry of the
